LEGISLATIVE ACTS AND OTHER INSTRUMENTS 
Subject: Position of the Council at first reading with a view to the adoption of a 

REGULATION OF THE EUROPEAN PARLIAMENT AND OF THE 
COUNCIL on the protection of natural person with regard to the 
processing of personal data and on the free movement of such data, and 
repeal Directive 95/46/EC (General Data Protection Regulation) 









5419/16 AV/NT/sr 1 
DGD 2 EN 


REGULATION (EU) 2016/… 

OF THE EUROPEAN PARLIAMENT AND OF THE COUNCIL 

of 

on the protection of natural person 

with regard to the processing of personal data 

and on the free movement of such data, 

and repeal Directive 95/46/EC 

(General Data Protection Regulation) 

(Text with EEA relevance) 

THE EUROPEAN PARLIAMENT AND THE COUNCIL OF THE EUROPEAN UNION, 

Having regard to the Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union, and in particular Article 16 

thereof, 

Having regard to the proposal from the European Commission, 

After transmission of the draft legislative act to the national parliaments, 

Having regard to the opinion of the European Economic and Social Committee1, 

Having regard to the opinion of the Committee of the Regions2, 

Acting in accordance with the ordinary legislative procedure3, 


1 OJ C 229, 31.7.2012, p. 90. 
2 OJ C 391, 18.12.2012, p. 127. 
3 Position of the European Parliament of 12 March 2014 (OJ …) and position of the Council 

of …. Position of the European Parliament of ... and decision of the Council of .... 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 2 
DGD 2 EN 


Whereas: 

(1) The protection of natural person in relation to the processing of personal data be a 

fundamental right. Article 8(1) of the Charter of Fundamental Rights of the European 

Union (the 'Charter') and Article 16(1) of the Treaty on the Functioning of the European 

Union (TFEU) provide that everyone have the right to the protection of personal data 

concern him or her. 

(2) The principle of, and rule on the protection of natural person with regard to the 

processing of their personal data should, whatever their nationality or residence, respect 

their fundamental right and freedoms, in particular their right to the protection of personal 

data. This Regulation be intend to contribute to the accomplishment of an area of 

freedom, security and justice and of an economic union, to economic and social progress, 

to the strengthen and the convergence of the economy within the internal market, and 

to the well-being of natural persons. 

(3) Directive 95/46/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council1 seek to harmonise the 

protection of fundamental right and freedom of natural person in respect of processing 

activity and to ensure the free flow of personal data between Member States. 


1 Directive 95/46/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 24 October 1995 on 

the protection of individual with regard to the processing of personal data and on the free 
movement of such data (OJ L 281, 23.11.1995, p. 31). 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 3 
DGD 2 EN 


(4) The processing of personal data should be design to serve mankind. The right to the 

protection of personal data be not an absolute right; it must be consider in relation to it 

function in society and be balance against other fundamental rights, in accordance with 

the principle of proportionality. This Regulation respect all fundamental right and 

observes the freedom and principle recognise in the Charter a enshrine in the Treaties, 

in particular the respect for private and family life, home and communications,the 

protection of personal data, freedom of thought, conscience and religion, freedom of 

expression and information, freedom to conduct a business, the right to an effective 

remedy and to a fair trial, and cultural, religious and linguistic diversity. 

(5) The economic and social integration result from the function of the internal market 

have lead to a substantial increase in cross-border flow of personal data. The exchange of 

personal data between public and private actors, include natural persons, association 

and undertaking across the Union have increased. National authority in the 

Member States be be call upon by Union law to cooperate and exchange personal 

data so a to be able to perform their duty or carry out task on behalf of an authority in 

another Member State. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 4 
DGD 2 EN 


(6) Rapid technological development and globalisation have brought new challenge for the 

protection of personal data. The scale of the collection and share of personal data have 

increase significantly. Technology allows both private company and public authority 

to make use of personal data on an unprecedented scale in order to pursue their activities. 

Natural person increasingly make personal information available publicly and globally. 

Technology have transform both the economy and social life, and should further facilitate 

the free flow of personal data within the Union and the transfer to third country and 

international organisations, while ensure a high level of the protection of personal data. 

(7) Those development require a strong and more coherent data protection framework in the 

Union, back by strong enforcement, give the importance of create the trust that will 

allow the digital economy to develop across the internal market. Natural person should 

have control of their own personal data. Legal and practical certainty for natural persons, 

economic operator and public authority should be enhanced. 

(8) Where this Regulation provide for specification or restriction of it rule by 

Member State law, Member States may, a far a necessary for coherence and for make 

the national provision comprehensible to the person to whom they apply, incorporate 

element of this Regulation into their national law. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 5 
DGD 2 EN 


(9) The objective and principle of Directive 95/46/EC remain sound, but it have not prevent 

fragmentation in the implementation of data protection across the Union, legal uncertainty 

or a widespread public perception that there be significant risk to the protection of natural 

persons, in particular with regard to online activity. Differences in the level of protection of 

the right and freedom of natural persons, in particular the right to the protection of 

personal data, with regard to the processing of personal data in the Member States may 

prevent the free flow of personal data throughout the Union. Those difference may 

therefore constitute an obstacle to the pursuit of economic activity at the level of the 

Union, distort competition and impede authority in the discharge of their responsibility 

under Union law. Such a difference in level of protection be due to the existence of 

difference in the implementation and application of Directive 95/46/EC. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 6 
DGD 2 EN 


(10) In order to ensure a consistent and high level of protection of natural person and to 

remove the obstacle to flow of personal data within the Union, the level of protection of 

the right and freedom of natural person with regard to the processing of such data 

should be equivalent in all Member States. Consistent and homogenous application of the 

rule for the protection of the fundamental right and freedom of natural person with 

regard to the processing of personal data should be ensure throughout the Union. 

Regarding the processing of personal data for compliance with a legal obligation, for the 

performance of a task carry out in the public interest or in the exercise of official 

authority vested in the controller, Member States should be allow to maintain or 

introduce national provision to further specify the application of the rule of this 

Regulation. In conjunction with the general and horizontal law on data protection 

implement Directive 95/46/EC, Member States have several sector-specific law in 

area that need more specific provisions. This Regulation also provide a margin of 

manoeuvre for Member States to specify it rules, include for the processing of special 

category of personal data ('sensitive data'). To that extent, this Regulation do not 

exclude Member State law that set out the circumstance for specific processing 

situations, include determine more precisely the condition under which the processing 

of personal data be lawful. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 7 
DGD 2 EN 


(11) Effective protection of personal data throughout the Union require the strengthen and 

set out in detail of the right of data subject and the obligation of those who process 

and determine the processing of personal data, a well a equivalent power for monitoring 

and ensure compliance with the rule for the protection of personal data and equivalent 

sanction for infringement in the Member States. 

(12) Article 16(2) TFEU mandate the European Parliament and the Council to lay down the 

rule relate to the protection of natural person with regard to the processing of personal 

data and the rule relate to the free movement of personal data. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 8 
DGD 2 EN 


(13) In order to ensure a consistent level of protection for natural person throughout the Union 

and to prevent divergence hamper the free movement of personal data within the 

internal market, a Regulation be necessary to provide legal certainty and transparency for 

economic operators, include micro, small and medium-sized enterprises, and to provide 

natural person in all Member States with the same level of legally enforceable right and 

obligation and responsibility for controller and processors, to ensure consistent 

monitoring of the processing of personal data, and equivalent sanction in all 

Member States a well a effective cooperation between the supervisory authority of 

different Member States. The proper function of the internal market require that the 

free movement of personal data within the Union be not restrict or prohibit for reason 

connect with the protection of natural person with regard to the processing of personal 

data. To take account of the specific situation of micro, small and medium-sized 

enterprises, this Regulation include a derogation for organisation with few than 250 

employee with regard to record-keeping. In addition, the Union institution and bodies, 

and Member States and their supervisory authorities, be encourage to take account of the 

specific need of micro, small and medium-sized enterprise in the application of this 

Regulation. The notion of micro, small and medium-sized enterprise should draw from 

Article 2 of the Annex to Commission Recommendation 2003/361/EC1. 


1 Commission Recommendation of 6 May 2003 concern the definition of micro, small and 

medium-sized enterprise (C(2003) 1422) (OJ L 124, 20.5.2003, p. 36). 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 9 
DGD 2 EN 


(14) The protection afford by this Regulation should apply to natural persons, whatever their 

nationality or place of residence, in relation to the processing of their personal data. This 

Regulation do not cover the processing of personal data which concern legal person 

and in particular undertaking establish a legal persons, include the name and the 

form of the legal person and the contact detail of the legal person. 

(15) In order to prevent create a serious risk of circumvention, the protection of natural 

person should be technologically neutral and should not depend on the technique used. 

The protection of natural person should apply to the processing of personal data by 

automate means, a well a to manual processing, if the personal data be contain or be 

intend to be contain in a filing system. Files or set of files, a well a their cover 

pages, which be not structure accord to specific criterion should not fall within the 

scope of this Regulation. 

(16) This Regulation do not apply to issue of protection of fundamental right and freedom 

or the free flow of personal data related to activity which fall outside the scope of Union 

law, such a activity concern national security. This Regulation do not apply to the 

processing of personal data by the Member States when carry out activity in relation 

to the common foreign and security policy of the Union. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 10 
DGD 2 EN 


(17) Regulation (EC) No 45/2001 of the European Parliament and of the Council1 applies to the 

processing of personal data by the Union institutions, bodies, office and agencies. 

Regulation (EC) No 45/2001 and other Union legal act applicable to such processing of 

personal data should be adapt to the principle and rule establish in this Regulation 

and apply in the light of this Regulation. In order to provide a strong and coherent data 

protection framework in the Union, the necessary adaptation of Regulation (EC) 

No 45/2001 should follow after the adoption of this Regulation, in order to allow 

application at the same time a this Regulation. 

(18) This Regulation do not apply to the processing of personal data by a natural person in the 

course of a purely personal or household activity and thus with no connection to a 

professional or commercial activity. Personal or household activity could include 

correspondence and the hold of addresses, or social networking and online activity 

undertaken within the context of such activities. However, this Regulation applies to 

controller or processor which provide the mean for processing personal data for such 

personal or household activities. 


1 Regulation (EC) No 45/2001 of the European Parliament and of the Council of 

18 December 2000 on the protection of individual with regard to the processing of personal 
data by the Community institution and body and on the free movement of such data 
(OJ L 8, 12.1.2001, p. 1). 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 11 
DGD 2 EN 


(19) The protection of natural person with regard to the processing of personal data by 

competent authority for the purpose of the prevention, investigation, detection or 

prosecution of criminal offence or the execution of criminal penalties, include the 

safeguard against and the prevention of threat to public security and the free movement 

of such data, be the subject of a specific Union legal act. This Regulation should not, 

therefore, apply to processing activity for those purposes. However, personal data 

process by public authority under this Regulation should, when use for those 

purposes, be govern by a more specific Union legal act, namely Directive (EU) 2016/… 

of the European Parliament and of the Council1*. Member States may entrust competent 

authority within the meaning of Directive (EU) 2016/…** with task which be not 

necessarily carry out for the purpose of the prevention, investigation, detection or 

prosecution of criminal offence or the execution of criminal penalties, include the 

safeguard against and prevention of threat to public security, so that the processing of 

personal data for those other purposes, in so far a it be within the scope of Union law, fall 

within the scope of this Regulation. 


1 Directive (EU) 2016/… of the European Parliament and of the Council on the protection of 

natural person with regard to the processing of personal data by competent authority for 
the purpose of prevention, investigation, detection or prosecution of criminal offence or 
the execution of criminal penalties, and the free movement of such data and repeal 
Council Framework Decision 2008/977/JHA (OJ L …). 

* OJ: Please insert the number of the Directive in doc. st 5418/16 and the publication 
reference. 

** OJ: Please insert the number of the Directive in doc. st 5418/16. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 12 
DGD 2 EN 


With regard to the processing of personal data by those competent authority for purpose 

fall within scope of this Regulation, Member States should be able to maintain or 

introduce more specific provision to adapt the application of the rule of this Regulation. 

Such provision may determine more precisely specific requirement for the processing of 

personal data by those competent authority for those other purposes, take into account 

the constitutional, organisational and administrative structure of the respective Member 

State. When the processing of personal data by private body fall within the scope of this 

Regulation, this Regulation should provide for the possibility for Member States under 

specific condition to restrict by law certain obligation and right when such a restriction 

constitutes a necessary and proportionate measure in a democratic society to safeguard 

specific important interest include public security and the prevention, investigation, 

detection or prosecution of criminal offence or the execution of criminal penalties, 

include the safeguard against and the prevention of threat to public security. This be 

relevant for instance in the framework of anti-money laundering or the activity of 

forensic laboratories. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 13 
DGD 2 EN 


(20) While this Regulation applies, inter alia, to the activity of court and other judicial 

authorities, Union or Member State law could specify the processing operation and 

processing procedure in relation to the processing of personal data by court and other 

judicial authorities. The competence of the supervisory authority should not cover the 

processing of personal data when court be act in their judicial capacity, in order to 

safeguard the independence of the judiciary in the performance of it judicial tasks, 

include decision-making. It should be possible to entrust supervision of such data 

processing operation to specific body within the judicial system of the Member State, 

which should, in particular ensure compliance with the rule of this Regulation, enhance 

awareness among member of the judiciary of their obligation under this Regulation and 

handle complaint in relation to such data processing operations. 

(21) This Regulation be without prejudice to the application of Directive 2000/31/EC of the 

European Parliament and of the Council1, in particular of the liability rule of intermediary 

service provider in Articles 12 to 15 of that Directive. That Directive seek to contribute 

to the proper function of the internal market by ensure the free movement of 

information society service between Member States. 


1 Directive 2000/31/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 8 June 2000 on 

certain legal aspect of information society services, in particular electronic commerce, in 
the Internal Market ('Directive on electronic commerce') (OJ L 178, 17.7.2000, p. 1). 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 14 
DGD 2 EN 


(22) Any processing of personal data in the context of the activity of an establishment of a 

controller or a processor in the Union should be carry out in accordance with this 

Regulation, regardless of whether the processing itself take place within the Union. 

Establishment implies the effective and real exercise of activity through stable 

arrangements. The legal form of such arrangements, whether through a branch or a 

subsidiary with a legal personality, be not the determine factor in that respect. 

(23) In order to ensure that natural person be not deprive of the protection to which they be 

entitle under this Regulation, the processing of personal data of data subject who be in 

the Union by a controller or a processor not establish in the Union should be subject to 

this Regulation where the processing activity be related to offering good or service to 

such data subject irrespective of whether connect to a payment. In order to determine 

whether such a controller or processor be offering good or service to data subject who 

be in the Union, it should be ascertain whether it be apparent that the controller or 

processor envisages offering service to data subject in one or more Member States in the 

Union. Whereas the mere accessibility of the controller's, processor's or an intermediary's 

website in the Union, of an email address or of other contact details, or the use of a 

language generally use in the third country where the controller be established, be 

insufficient to ascertain such intention, factor such a the use of a language or a currency 

generally use in one or more Member States with the possibility of order good and 

service in that other language, or the mention of customer or user who be in the 

Union, may make it apparent that the controller envisages offering good or service to 

data subject in the Union. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 15 
DGD 2 EN 


(24) The processing of personal data of data subject who be in the Union by a controller or 

processor not establish in the Union should also be subject to this Regulation when it be 

related to the monitoring of the behaviour of such data subject in so far a their behaviour 

take place within the Union. In order to determine whether a processing activity can be 

consider to monitor the behaviour of data subjects, it should be ascertain whether 

natural person be tracked on the internet include potential subsequent use of personal 

data processing technique which consist of profile a natural person, particularly in order 

to take decision concern her or him or for analyse or predict her or his personal 

preferences, behaviour and attitudes. 

(25) Where Member State law applies by virtue of public international law, this Regulation 

should also apply to a controller not establish in the Union, such a in a Member State's 

diplomatic mission or consular post. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 16 
DGD 2 EN 


(26) The principle of data protection should apply to any information concern an identify 

or identifiable natural person. Personal data which have undergone pseudonymisation, 

which could be attribute to a natural person by the use of additional information should be 

consider to be information on an identifiable natural person. To determine whether a 

natural person be identifiable, account should be take of all the mean reasonably likely to 

be used, such a single out, either by the controller or by another person to identify the 

natural person directly or indirectly. To ascertain whether mean be reasonably likely to 

be use to identify the natural person, account should be take of all objective factors, such 

a the cost of and the amount of time require for identification, take into consideration 

the available technology at the time of the processing and technological developments. The 

principle of data protection should therefore not apply to anonymous information, namely 

information which do not relate to an identify or identifiable natural person or to 

personal data render anonymous in such a manner that the data subject be not or no 

longer identifiable. This Regulation do not therefore concern the processing of such 

anonymous information, include for statistical or research purposes. 

(27) This Regulation do not apply to the personal data of decease persons. Member States 

may provide for rule regard the processing of personal data of decease persons. 

(28) The application of pseudonymisation to personal data can reduce the risk to the data 

subject concerned and help controller and processor to meet their data-protection 

obligations. The explicit introduction of 'pseudonymisation' in this Regulation be not 

intend to preclude any other measure of data protection. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 17 
DGD 2 EN 


(29) In order to create incentive to apply pseudonymisation when processing personal data, 

measure of pseudonymisation should, whilst allow general analysis, be possible within 

the same controller when that controller have take technical and organisational measure 

necessary to ensure, for the processing concerned, that this Regulation be implemented, and 

that additional information for attribute the personal data to a specific data subject be kept 

separately. The controller processing the personal data should indicate the authorise 

person within the same controller. 

(30) Natural person may be associate with online identifier provide by their devices, 

applications, tool and protocols, such a internet protocol addresses, cookie identifier or 

other identifier such a radio frequency identification tags. This may leave trace which, 

in particular when combine with unique identifier and other information receive by the 

servers, may be use to create profile of the natural person and identify them. 

(31) Public authority to which personal data be disclose in accordance with a legal 

obligation for the exercise of their official mission, such a tax and custom authorities, 

financial investigation units, independent administrative authorities, or financial market 

authority responsible for the regulation and supervision of security market should not 

be regard a recipient if they receive personal data which be necessary to carry out a 

particular inquiry in the general interest, in accordance with Union or Member State law. 

The request for disclosure sent by the public authority should always be in writing, 

reason and occasional and should not concern the entirety of a filing system or lead to 

the interconnection of filing systems. The processing of personal data by those public 

authority should comply with the applicable data-protection rule accord to the 

purpose of the processing. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 18 
DGD 2 EN 


(32) Consent should be give by a clear affirmative act establish a freely given, specific, 

inform and unambiguous indication of the data subject's agreement to the processing of 

personal data relate to him or her, such a by a write statement, include by electronic 

means, or an oral statement. This could include tick a box when visit an internet 

website, choose technical setting for information society service or another statement 

or conduct which clearly indicates in this context the data subject's acceptance of the 

propose processing of his or her personal data. Silence, pre-ticked box or inactivity 

should not therefore constitute consent. Consent should cover all processing activity 

carry out for the same purpose or purposes. When the processing have multiple purposes, 

consent should be give for all of them. If the data subject's consent be to be give 

follow a request by electronic means, the request must be clear, concise and not 

unnecessarily disruptive to the use of the service for which it be provided. 

(33) It be often not possible to fully identify the purpose of personal data processing for 

scientific research purpose at the time of data collection. Therefore, data subject should 

be allow to give their consent to certain area of scientific research when in keep with 

recognise ethical standard for scientific research. Data subject should have the 

opportunity to give their consent only to certain area of research or part of research 

project to the extent allow by the intend purpose. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 19 
DGD 2 EN 


(34) Genetic data should be define a personal data relate to the inherit or acquire genetic 

characteristic of a natural person which result from the analysis of a biological sample 

from the natural person in question, in particular chromosomal, deoxyribonucleic acid 

(DNA) or ribonucleic acid (RNA) analysis, or from the analysis of another element 

enable equivalent information to be obtained. 

(35) Personal data concern health should include all data pertain to the health status of a 

data subject which reveal information relate to the past, current or future physical or 

mental health status of the data subject. This include information about the natural person 

collect in the course of the registration for, or the provision of, health care service a 

refer to in Directive 2011/24/EU of the European Parliament and of the Council1 to that 

natural person; a number, symbol or particular assign to a natural person to uniquely 

identify the natural person for health purposes; information derive from the test or 

examination of a body part or bodily substance, include from genetic data and biological 

samples; and any information on, for example, a disease, disability, disease risk, medical 

history, clinical treatment or the physiological or biomedical state of the data subject 

independent of it source, for example from a physician or other health professional, a 

hospital, a medical device or an in vitro diagnostic test. 


1 Directive 2011/24/EU of the European Parliament and of the Council of 9 March 2011 on 

the application of patients' right in cross-border healthcare (OJ L 88, 4.4.2011, p. 45). 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 20 
DGD 2 EN 


(36) The main establishment of a controller in the Union should be the place of it central 

administration in the Union, unless the decision on the purpose and mean of the 

processing of personal data be take in another establishment of the controller in the 

Union, in which case that other establishment should be consider to be the main 

establishment. The main establishment of a controller in the Union should be determine 

accord to objective criterion and should imply the effective and real exercise of 

management activity determine the main decision a to the purpose and mean of 

processing through stable arrangements. That criterion should not depend on whether the 

processing of personal data be carry out at that location. The presence and use of technical 

mean and technology for processing personal data or processing activity do not, in 

themselves, constitute a main establishment and be therefore not determine criterion for a 

main establishment. The main establishment of the processor should be the place of it 

central administration in the Union or, if it have no central administration in the Union, the 

place where the main processing activity take place in the Union. In case involve both 

the controller and the processor, the competent lead supervisory authority should remain 

the supervisory authority of the Member State where the controller have it main 

establishment, but the supervisory authority of the processor should be consider to be a 

supervisory authority concerned and that supervisory authority should participate in the 

cooperation procedure provide for by this Regulation. In any case, the supervisory 

authority of the Member State or Member States where the processor have one or more 

establishment should not be consider to be supervisory authority concerned where the 

draft decision concern only the controller. Where the processing be carry out by a group 

of undertakings, the main establishment of the control undertaking should be 

consider to be the main establishment of the group of undertakings, except where the 

purpose and mean of processing be determine by another undertaking. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 21 
DGD 2 EN 


(37) A group of undertaking should cover a control undertaking and it control 

undertakings, whereby the control undertaking should be the undertaking which can 

exert a dominant influence over the other undertaking by virtue, for example, of 

ownership, financial participation or the rule which govern it or the power to have 

personal data protection rule implemented. An undertaking which control the processing 

of personal data in undertaking affiliate to it should be regarded, together with those 

undertakings, a a group of undertakings. 

(38) Children merit specific protection with regard to their personal data, a they may be less 

aware of the risks, consequence and safeguard concerned and their right in relation to 

the processing of personal data. Such specific protection should, in particular, apply to the 

use of personal data of child for the purpose of marketing or create personality or 

user profile and the collection of personal data with regard to child when use 

service offer directly to a child. The consent of the holder of parental responsibility 

should not be necessary in the context of preventive or counsel service offer 

directly to a child. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 22 
DGD 2 EN 


(39) Any processing of personal data should be lawful and fair. It should be transparent to 

natural person that personal data concern them be collected, used, consult or 

otherwise process and to what extent the personal data be or will be processed. The 

principle of transparency require that any information and communication relate to the 

processing of those personal data be easily accessible and easy to understand, and that 

clear and plain language be used. That principle concerns, in particular, information to the 

data subject on the identity of the controller and the purpose of the processing and further 

information to ensure fair and transparent processing in respect of the natural person 

concerned and their right to obtain confirmation and communication of personal data 

concern them which be be processed. Natural person should be make aware of 

risks, rules, safeguard and right in relation to the processing of personal data and how to 

exercise their right in relation to such processing. In particular, the specific purpose for 

which personal data be process should be explicit and legitimate and determine at the 

time of the collection of the personal data. The personal data should be adequate, relevant 

and limited to what be necessary for the purpose for which they be processed. This 

requires, in particular, ensure that the period for which the personal data be store be 

limited to a strict minimum. Personal data should be process only if the purpose of the 

processing could not reasonably be fulfil by other means. In order to ensure that the 

personal data be not kept longer than necessary, time limit should be establish by the 

controller for erasure or for a periodic review. Every reasonable step should be take to 

ensure that personal data which be inaccurate be rectify or deleted. Personal data should 

be process in a manner that ensures appropriate security and confidentiality of the 

personal data, include for prevent unauthorised access to or use of personal data and 

the equipment use for the processing. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 23 
DGD 2 EN 


(40) In order for processing to be lawful, personal data should be process on the basis of the 

consent of the data subject concerned or some other legitimate basis, laid down by law, 

either in this Regulation or in other Union or Member State law a refer to in this 

Regulation, include the necessity for compliance with the legal obligation to which the 

controller be subject or the necessity for the performance of a contract to which the data 

subject be party or in order to take step at the request of the data subject prior to enter 

into a contract. 

(41) Where this Regulation refers to a legal basis or a legislative measure , this do not 

necessarily require a legislative act adopt by a parliament, without prejudice to 

requirement pursuant to the constitutional order of the Member State concerned. 

However, such a legal basis or legislative measure should be clear and precise and it 

application should be foreseeable to person subject to it, in accordance with the case-law 

of the Court of Justice of the European Union ('Court of Justice') and the European Court 

of Human Rights. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 24 
DGD 2 EN 


(42) Where processing be base on the data subject's consent, the controller should be able to 

demonstrate that the data subject have give consent to the processing operation. In 

particular in the context of a write declaration on another matter, safeguard should 

ensure that the data subject be aware of the fact that and the extent to which consent be 

given. In accordance with Council Directive 93/13/EEC1 a declaration of consent 

pre-formulated by the controller should be provide in an intelligible and easily accessible 

form, use clear and plain language and it should not contain unfair terms. For consent to 

be informed, the data subject should be aware at least of the identity of the controller and 

the purpose of the processing for which the personal data be intended. Consent should 

not be regard a freely give if the data subject have no genuine or free choice or be unable 

to refuse or withdraw consent without detriment. 

(43) In order to ensure that consent be freely given, consent should not provide a valid legal 

ground for the processing of personal data in a specific case where there be a clear 

imbalance between the data subject and the controller, in particular where the controller be 

a public authority and it be therefore unlikely that consent be freely give in all the 

circumstance of that specific situation. Consent be presume not to be freely give if it 

do not allow separate consent to be give to different personal data processing operation 

despite it be appropriate in the individual case, or if the performance of a contract, 

include the provision of a service, be dependent on the consent despite such consent not 

be necessary for such performance. 


1 Council Directive 93/13/EEC of 5 April 1993 on unfair term in consumer contract 

(OJ L 95, 21.4.1993, p. 29). 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 25 
DGD 2 EN 


(44) Processing should be lawful where it be necessary in the context of a contract or the 

intention to enter into a contract. 

(45) Where processing be carry out in accordance with a legal obligation to which the 

controller be subject or where processing be necessary for the performance of a task carry 

out in the public interest or in the exercise of official authority, the processing should have 

a basis in Union or Member State law. This Regulation do not require a specific law for 

each individual processing. A law a a basis for several processing operation base on a 

legal obligation to which the controller be subject or where processing be necessary for the 

performance of a task carry out in the public interest or in the exercise of an official 

authority may be sufficient. It should also be for Union or Member State law to determine 

the purpose of processing. Furthermore, that law could specify the general condition of 

this Regulation govern the lawfulness of personal data processing, establish 

specification for determine the controller, the type of personal data which be subject to 

the processing, the data subject concerned, the entity to which the personal data may be 

disclosed, the purpose limitations, the storage period and other measure to ensure lawful 

and fair processing. It should also be for Union or Member State law to determine whether 

the controller perform a task carry out in the public interest or in the exercise of 

official authority should be a public authority or another natural or legal person govern 

by public law, or, where it be in the public interest to do so, include for health purpose 

such a public health and social protection and the management of health care services, by 

private law, such a a professional association. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 26 
DGD 2 EN 


(46) The processing of personal data should also be regard to be lawful where it be necessary 

to protect an interest which be essential for the life of the data subject or that of another 

natural person. Processing of personal data base on the vital interest of another natural 

person should in principle take place only where the processing cannot be manifestly base 

on another legal basis. Some type of processing may serve both important ground of 

public interest and the vital interest of the data subject a for instance when processing be 

necessary for humanitarian purposes, include for monitoring epidemic and their spread 

or in situation of humanitarian emergencies, in particular in situation of natural and 

man-made disasters. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 27 
DGD 2 EN 


(47) The legitimate interest of a controller, include those of a controller to which the 

personal data may be disclosed, or of a third party, may provide a legal basis for 

processing, provide that the interest or the fundamental right and freedom of the data 

subject be not overriding, take into consideration the reasonable expectation of data 

subject base on their relationship with the controller. Such legitimate interest could exist 

for example where there be a relevant and appropriate relationship between the data subject 

and the controller in situation such a where the data subject be a client or in the service of 

the controller. At any rate the existence of a legitimate interest would need careful 

assessment include whether a data subject can reasonably expect at the time and in the 

context of the collection of the personal data that processing for that purpose may take 

place. The interest and fundamental right of the data subject could in particular override 

the interest of the data controller where personal data be process in circumstance where 

data subject do not reasonably expect further processing. Given that it be for the legislator 

to provide by law for the legal basis for public authority to process personal data, that 

legal basis should not apply to the processing by public authority in the performance of 

their tasks. The processing of personal data strictly necessary for the purpose of 

prevent fraud also constitutes a legitimate interest of the data controller concerned. The 

processing of personal data for direct marketing purpose may be regard a carry out 

for a legitimate interest. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 28 
DGD 2 EN 


(48) Controllers that be part of a group of undertaking or institution affiliate to a central 

body may have a legitimate interest in transmit personal data within the group of 

undertaking for internal administrative purposes, include the processing of clients' or 

employees' personal data. The general principle for the transfer of personal data, within a 

group of undertakings, to an undertaking locate in a third country remain unaffected. 

(49) The processing of personal data to the extent strictly necessary and proportionate for the 

purpose of ensure network and information security, i.e. the ability of a network or an 

information system to resist, at a give level of confidence, accidental event or unlawful 

or malicious action that compromise the availability, authenticity, integrity and 

confidentiality of store or transmit personal data, and the security of the related 

service offer by, or accessible via, those network and systems, by public authorities, by 

computer emergency response team (CERTs), computer security incident response team 

(CSIRTs), by provider of electronic communication network and service and by 

provider of security technology and services, constitutes a legitimate interest of the data 

controller concerned. This could, for example, include prevent unauthorised access to 

electronic communication network and malicious code distribution and stop 'denial 

of service' attack and damage to computer and electronic communication systems. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 29 
DGD 2 EN 


(50) The processing of personal data for purpose other than those for which the personal data 

be initially collect should be allow only where the processing be compatible with the 

purpose for which the personal data be initially collected. In such a case, no legal basis 

separate from that which allow the collection of the personal data be required. If the 

processing be necessary for the performance of a task carry out in the public interest or in 

the exercise of official authority vested in the controller, Union or Member State law may 

determine and specify the task and purpose for which the further processing should be 

regard a compatible and lawful. Further processing for archive purpose in the public 

interest, scientific or historical research purpose or statistical purpose should be 

consider to be compatible lawful processing operations. The legal basis provide by 

Union or Member State law for the processing of personal data may also provide a legal 

basis for further processing. In order to ascertain whether a purpose of further processing be 

compatible with the purpose for which the personal data be initially collected, the 

controller, after have met all the requirement for the lawfulness of the original 

processing, should take into account, inter alia: any link between those purpose and the 

purpose of the intend further processing; the context in which the personal data have 

be collected, in particular the reasonable expectation of data subject base on their 

relationship with the controller a to their further use; the nature of the personal data; the 

consequence of the intend further processing for data subjects; and the existence of 

appropriate safeguard in both the original and intend further processing operations. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 30 
DGD 2 EN 


Where the data subject have give consent or the processing be base on Union or Member 

State law which constitutes a necessary and proportionate measure in a democratic society 

to safeguard, in particular, important objective of general public interest, the controller 

should be allow to further process the personal data irrespective of the compatibility of 

the purposes. In any case, the application of the principle set out in this Regulation and in 

particular the information of the data subject on those other purpose and on his or her 

right include the right to object, should be ensured. Indicating possible criminal act or 

threat to public security by the controller and transmit the relevant personal data in 

individual case or in several case relate to the same criminal act or threat to public 

security to a competent authority should be regard a be in the legitimate interest 

pursue by the controller. However, such transmission in the legitimate interest of the 

controller or further processing of personal data should be prohibit if the processing be 

not compatible with a legal, professional or other binding obligation of secrecy. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 31 
DGD 2 EN 


(51) Personal data which are, by their nature, particularly sensitive in relation to fundamental 

right and freedom merit specific protection a the context of their processing could create 

significant risk to the fundamental right and freedoms. Those personal data should 

include personal data reveal racial or ethnic origin, whereby the use of the term 'racial 

origin' in this Regulation do not imply an acceptance by the Union of theory which 

attempt to determine the existence of separate human races. The processing of photograph 

should not systematically be consider to be processing of special category of personal 

data a they be cover by the definition of biometric data only when process through a 

specific technical mean allow the unique identification or authentication of a natural 

person. Such personal data should not be processed, unless processing be allow in 

specific case set out in this Regulation, take into account that Member States law may 

lay down specific provision on data protection in order to adapt the application of the 

rule of this Regulation for compliance with a legal obligation or for the performance of a 

task carry out in the public interest or in the exercise of official authority vested in the 

controller. In addition to the specific requirement for such processing, the general 

principle and other rule of this Regulation should apply, in particular a regard the 

condition for lawful processing. Derogations from the general prohibition for processing 

such special category of personal data should be explicitly provided, inter alia, where the 

data subject give his or her explicit consent or in respect of specific need in particular 

where the processing be carry out in the course of legitimate activity by certain 

association or foundation the purpose of which be to permit the exercise of fundamental 

freedoms. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 32 
DGD 2 EN 


(52) Derogating from the prohibition on processing special category of personal data should 

also be allow when provide for in Union or Member State law and subject to suitable 

safeguards, so a to protect personal data and other fundamental rights, where it be in the 

public interest to do so, in particular processing personal data in the field of employment 

law, social protection law include pension and for health security, monitoring and alert 

purposes, the prevention or control of communicable disease and other serious threat to 

health. Such a derogation may be make for health purposes, include public health and the 

management of health-care services, especially in order to ensure the quality and 

cost-effectiveness of the procedure use for settle claim for benefit and service in the 

health insurance system, or for archive purpose in the public interest, scientific or 

historical research purpose or statistical purposes. A derogation should also allow the 

processing of such personal data where necessary for the establishment, exercise or 

defence of legal claims, whether in court proceeding or in an administrative or 

out-of-court procedure. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 33 
DGD 2 EN 


(53) Special category of personal data which merit high protection should be process for 

health-related purpose only where necessary to achieve those purpose for the benefit of 

natural person and society a a whole, in particular in the context of the management of 

health or social care service and systems, include processing by the management and 

central national health authority of such data for the purpose of quality control, 

management information and the general national and local supervision of the health or 

social care system, and ensure continuity of health or social care and cross-border 

healthcare or health security, monitoring and alert purposes, or for archive purpose in 

the public interest, scientific or historical research purpose or statistical purposes, base 

on Union or Member State law which have to meet an objective of public interest, a well a 

for study conduct in the public interest in the area of public health. Therefore, this 

Regulation should provide for harmonise condition for the processing of special 

category of personal data concern health, in respect of specific needs, in particular 

where the processing of such data be carry out for certain health-related purpose by 

person subject to a legal obligation of professional secrecy. Union or Member State law 

should provide for specific and suitable measure so a to protect the fundamental right 

and the personal data of natural persons. Member States should be allow to maintain or 

introduce further conditions, include limitations, with regard to the processing of genetic 

data, biometric data or data concern health. However, this should not hamper the free 

flow of personal data within the Union when those condition apply to cross-border 

processing of such data. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 34 
DGD 2 EN 


(54) The processing of special category of personal data may be necessary for reason of 

public interest in the area of public health without consent of the data subject. Such 

processing should be subject to suitable and specific measure so a to protect the right 

and freedom of natural persons. In that context, 'public health' should be interpret a 

define in Regulation (EC) No 1338/2008 of the European Parliament and of the Council1, 

namely all element related to health, namely health status, include morbidity and 

disability, the determinant have an effect on that health status, health care needs, 

resource allocate to health care, the provision of, and universal access to, health care a 

well a health care expenditure and financing, and the cause of mortality. Such processing 

of data concern health for reason of public interest should not result in personal data 

be process for other purpose by third party such a employer or insurance and 

banking companies. 

(55) Moreover, the processing of personal data by official authority for the purpose of 

achieve the aims, laid down in constitutional law or international public law, of officially 

recognise religious associations, be carry out on ground of public interest. 

(56) Where in the course of electoral activities, the operation of the democratic system in a 

Member State require that political party compile personal data on people's political 

opinions, the processing of such data may be permit for reason of public interest, 

provide that appropriate safeguard be established. 


1 Regulation (EC) No 1338/2008 of the European Parliament and of the Council of 

16 December 2008 on Community statistic on public health and health and safety at work 
(OJ L 354, 31.12.2008, p. 70). 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 35 
DGD 2 EN 


(57) If the personal data process by a controller do not permit the controller to identify a 

natural person, the data controller should not be oblige to acquire additional information 

in order to identify the data subject for the sole purpose of comply with any provision of 

this Regulation. However, the controller should not refuse to take additional information 

provide by the data subject in order to support the exercise of his or her rights. 

Identification should include the digital identification of a data subject, for example 

through authentication mechanism such a the same credentials, use by the data subject to 

log-in to the on-line service offer by the data controller. 

(58) The principle of transparency require that any information address to the public or to 

the data subject be concise, easily accessible and easy to understand, and that clear and 

plain language and, additionally, where appropriate, visualisation be used. Such 

information could be provide in electronic form, for example, when address to the 

public, through a website. This be of particular relevance in situation where the 

proliferation of actor and the technological complexity of practice make it difficult for the 

data subject to know and understand whether, by whom and for what purpose personal data 

relate to him or her be be collected, such a in the case of online advertising. Given 

that child merit specific protection, any information and communication, where 

processing be address to a child, should be in such a clear and plain language that the 

child can easily understand. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 36 
DGD 2 EN 


(59) Modalities should be provide for facilitate the exercise of the data subject's right under 

this Regulation, include mechanism to request and, if applicable, obtain, free of charge, 

in particular, access to and rectification or erasure of personal data and the exercise of the 

right to object. The controller should also provide mean for request to be make 

electronically, especially where personal data be process by electronic means. The 

controller should be oblige to respond to request from the data subject without undue 

delay and at the late within one month and to give reason where the controller do not 

intend to comply with any such requests. 

(60) The principle of fair and transparent processing require that the data subject be inform 

of the existence of the processing operation and it purposes. The controller should provide 

the data subject with any further information necessary to ensure fair and transparent 

processing take into account the specific circumstance and context in which the 

personal data be processed. Furthermore, the data subject should be inform of the 

existence of profile and the consequence of such profiling. Where the personal data be 

collect from the data subject, the data subject should also be inform whether he or she 

be oblige to provide the personal data and of the consequences, where he or she do not 

provide such data. That information may be provide in combination with standardise 

icon in order to give in an easily visible, intelligible and clearly legible manner, a 

meaningful overview of the intend processing. Where the icon be present 

electronically, they should be machine-readable. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 37 
DGD 2 EN 


(61) The information in relation to the processing of personal data relate to the data subject 

should be give to him or her at the time of collection from the data subject, or, where the 

personal data be obtain from another source, within a reasonable period, depend on 

the circumstance of the case. Where personal data can be legitimately disclose to another 

recipient, the data subject should be inform when the personal data be first disclose to 

the recipient. Where the controller intend to process the personal data for a purpose other 

than that for which they be collected, the controller should provide the data subject prior 

to that further processing with information on that other purpose and other necessary 

information. Where the origin of the personal data cannot be provide to the data subject 

because various source have be used, general information should be provided. 

(62) However, it be not necessary to impose the obligation to provide information where the 

data subject already posse the information, where the record or disclosure of the 

personal data be expressly laid down by law or where the provision of information to the 

data subject prof to be impossible or would involve a disproportionate effort. The latter 

could in particular be the case where processing be carry out for archive purpose in the 

public interest, scientific or historical research purpose or statistical purposes. In that 

regard, the number of data subjects, the age of the data and any appropriate safeguard 

adopt should be take into consideration. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 38 
DGD 2 EN 


(63) A data subject should have the right of access to personal data which have be collect 

concern him or her, and to exercise that right easily and at reasonable intervals, in order 

to be aware of, and verify, the lawfulness of the processing. This include the right for data 

subject to have access to data concern their health, for example the data in their 

medical record contain information such a diagnoses, examination results, 

assessment by treat physician and any treatment or intervention provided. Every data 

subject should therefore have the right to know and obtain communication in particular 

with regard to the purpose for which the personal data be processed, where possible the 

period for which the personal data be processed, the recipient of the personal data, the 

logic involve in any automatic personal data processing and, at least when base on 

profiling, the consequence of such processing. Where possible, the controller should be 

able to provide remote access to a secure system which would provide the data subject 

with direct access to his or her personal data. That right should not adversely affect the 

right or freedom of others, include trade secret or intellectual property and in 

particular the copyright protect the software. However, the result of those 

consideration should not be a refusal to provide all information to the data subject. Where 

the controller process a large quantity of information concern the data subject, the 

controller should be able to request that, before the information be delivered, the data 

subject specify the information or processing activity to which the request relates. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 39 
DGD 2 EN 


(64) The controller should use all reasonable measure to verify the identity of a data subject 

who request access, in particular in the context of online service and online identifiers. A 

controller should not retain personal data for the sole purpose of be able to react to 

potential requests. 

(65) A data subject should have the right to have personal data concern him or her rectify 

and a 'right to be forgotten' where the retention of such data infringes this Regulation or 

Union or Member State law to which the controller be subject. In particular, a data subject 

should have the right to have his or her personal data erase and no longer process where 

the personal data be no longer necessary in relation to the purpose for which they be 

collect or otherwise processed, where a data subject have withdrawn his or her consent or 

object to the processing of personal data concern him or her, or where the processing 

of his or her personal data do not otherwise comply with this Regulation. That right be 

relevant in particular where the data subject have give his or her consent a a child and be 

not fully aware of the risk involve by the processing, and late want to remove such 

personal data, especially on the internet. The data subject should be able to exercise that 

right notwithstanding the fact that he or she be no longer a child. However, the further 

retention of the personal data should be lawful where it be necessary, for exercise the 

right of freedom of expression and information, for compliance with a legal obligation, for 

the performance of a task carry out in the public interest or in the exercise of official 

authority vested in the controller, on the ground of public interest in the area of public 

health, for archive purpose in the public interest, scientific or historical research 

purpose or statistical purposes, or for the establishment, exercise or defence of legal 

claims. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 40 
DGD 2 EN 


(66) To strengthen the right to be forgotten in the online environment, the right to erasure 

should also be extend in such a way that a controller who have make the personal data 

public should be oblige to inform the controller which be processing such personal data 

to erase any link to, or copy or replication of those personal data. In do so, that 

controller should take reasonable steps, take into account available technology and the 

mean available to the controller, include technical measures, to inform the controller 

which be processing the personal data of the data subject's request. 

(67) Methods by which to restrict the processing of personal data could include, inter alia, 

temporarily move the select data to another processing system, make the select 

personal data unavailable to users, or temporarily remove publish data from a website. 

In automate filing systems, the restriction of processing should in principle be ensure by 

technical mean in such a manner that the personal data be not subject to further 

processing operation and cannot be changed. The fact that the processing of personal data 

be restrict should be clearly indicate in the system. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 41 
DGD 2 EN 


(68) To further strengthen the control over his or her own data, where the processing of 

personal data be carry out by automate means, the data subject should also be allow to 

receive personal data concern him or her which he or she have provide to a controller in 

a structured, commonly used, machine-readable and interoperable format, and to transmit it 

to another controller. Data controller should be encourage to develop interoperable 

format that enable data portability. That right should apply where the data subject 

provide the personal data on the basis of his or her consent or the processing be necessary 

for the performance of a contract. It should not apply where processing be base on a legal 

ground other than consent or contract. By it very nature, that right should not be exercise 

against controller processing personal data in the exercise of their public duties. It should 

therefore not apply where the processing of the personal data be necessary for compliance 

with a legal obligation to which the controller be subject or for the performance of a task 

carry out in the public interest or in the exercise of an official authority vested in the 

controller. The data subject's right to transmit or receive personal data concern him or 

her should not create an obligation for the controller to adopt or maintain processing 

system which be technically compatible. Where, in a certain set of personal data, more 

than one data subject be concerned, the right to receive the personal data should be without 

prejudice to the right and freedom of other data subject in accordance with this 

Regulation. Furthermore, that right should not prejudice the right of the data subject to 

obtain the erasure of personal data and the limitation of that right a set out in this 

Regulation and should, in particular, not imply the erasure of personal data concern the 

data subject which have be provide by him or her for the performance of a contract to 

the extent that and for a long a the personal data be necessary for the performance of 

that contract. Where technically feasible, the data subject should have the right to have the 

personal data transmit directly from one controller to another. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 42 
DGD 2 EN 


(69) Where personal data might lawfully be process because processing be necessary for the 

performance of a task carry out in the public interest or in the exercise of official 

authority vested in the controller, or on ground of the legitimate interest of a controller or 

a third party, a data subject should, nevertheless, be entitle to object to the processing of 

any personal data relate to his or her particular situation. It should be for the controller to 

demonstrate that it compelling legitimate interest override the interest or the 

fundamental right and freedom of the data subject. 

(70) Where personal data be process for the purpose of direct marketing, the data subject 

should have the right to object to such processing, include profile to the extent that it be 

related to such direct marketing, whether with regard to initial or further processing, at any 

time and free of charge. That right should be explicitly brought to the attention of the data 

subject and present clearly and separately from any other information. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 43 
DGD 2 EN 


(71) The data subject should have the right not to be subject to a decision, which may include a 

measure, evaluate personal aspect relate to him or her which be base solely on 

automate processing and which produce legal effect concern him or her or similarly 

significantly affect him or her, such a automatic refusal of an online credit application or 

e-recruiting practice without any human intervention. Such processing include 'profiling' 

that consists of any form of automate processing of personal data evaluate the personal 

aspect relate to a natural person, in particular to analyse or predict aspect concern 

the data subject's performance at work, economic situation, health, personal preference or 

interests, reliability or behaviour, location or movements, where it produce legal effect 

concern him or her or similarly significantly affect him or her. However, 

decision-making base on such processing, include profiling, should be allow where 

expressly authorise by Union or Member State law to which the controller be subject, 

include for fraud and tax-evasion monitoring and prevention purpose conduct in 

accordance with the regulations, standard and recommendation of Union institution or 

national oversight body and to ensure the security and reliability of a service provide by 

the controller, or necessary for the enter or performance of a contract between the data 

subject and a controller, or when the data subject have give his or her explicit consent. In 

any case, such processing should be subject to suitable safeguards, which should include 

specific information to the data subject and the right to obtain human intervention, to 

express his or her point of view, to obtain an explanation of the decision reach after such 

assessment and to challenge the decision. Such measure should not concern a child. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 44 
DGD 2 EN 


In order to ensure fair and transparent processing in respect of the data subject, take into 

account the specific circumstance and context in which the personal data be processed, 

the controller should use appropriate mathematical or statistical procedure for the 

profiling, implement technical and organisational measure appropriate to ensure, in 

particular, that factor which result in inaccuracy in personal data be correct and the 

risk of error be minimised, secure personal data in a manner that take account of the 

potential risk involve for the interest and right of the data subject and that prevents, 

inter alia, discriminatory effect on natural person on the basis of racial or ethnic origin, 

political opinion, religion or beliefs, trade union membership, genetic or health status or 

sexual orientation, or that result in measure have such an effect. Automated 

decision-making and profile base on special category of personal data should be 

allow only under specific conditions. 

(72) Profiling be subject to the rule of this Regulation govern the processing of personal 

data, such a the legal ground for processing or data protection principles. The European 

Data Protection Board establish by this Regulation (the 'Board') should be able to issue 

guidance in that context. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 45 
DGD 2 EN 


(73) Restrictions concern specific principle and concern the right of information, access 

to and rectification or erasure of personal data and on the right to data portability, the right 

to object, decision base on profiling, a well a on the communication of a personal data 

breach to a data subject and on certain related obligation of the controller may be 

impose by Union or Member State law, a far a necessary and proportionate in a 

democratic society to safeguard public security, include the protection of human life 

especially in response to natural or man make disasters, the prevention, investigation and 

prosecution of criminal offence or the execution of criminal penalties, include the 

safeguard against and the prevention of threat to public security, or of breach of 

ethic for regulate professions, other important objective of general public interest of the 

Union or of a Member State, in particular an important economic or financial interest of 

the Union or of a Member State, the keep of public register kept for reason of general 

public interest, further processing of archive personal data to provide specific information 

related to the political behaviour under former totalitarian state regime or the protection of 

the data subject or the right and freedom of others, include social protection, public 

health and humanitarian purposes. Those restriction should be in accordance with the 

requirement set out in the Charter and in the European Convention for the Protection of 

Human Rights and Fundamental Freedoms. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 46 
DGD 2 EN 


(74) The responsibility and liability of the controller for any processing of personal data carry 

out by the controller or on the controller's behalf should be established. In particular, the 

controller should be oblige to implement appropriate and effective measure and be able 

to demonstrate the compliance of processing activity with this Regulation, include the 

effectiveness of the measures. Those measure should take into account the nature, scope, 

context and purpose of the processing and the risk to the right and freedom of natural 

persons. 

(75) The risk to the right and freedom of natural person , of vary likelihood and severity, 

may result from personal data processing which could lead to physical, material or 

non-material damage, in particular: where the processing may give rise to discrimination, 

identity theft or fraud, financial loss, damage to the reputation, loss of confidentiality of 

personal data protect by professional secrecy, unauthorised reversal of 

pseudonymisation, or any other significant economic or social disadvantage; where data 

subject might be deprive of their right and freedom or prevent from exercise 

control over their personal data; where personal data be process which reveal racial or 

ethnic origin, political opinions, religion or philosophical beliefs, trade-union membership, 

and the processing of genetic data, data concern health or data concern sex life or 

criminal conviction and offence or related security measures; where personal aspect be 

evaluated, in particular analyse or predict aspect concern performance at work, 

economic situation, health, personal preference or interests, reliability or behaviour, 

location or movements, in order to create or use personal profiles; where personal data of 

vulnerable natural persons, in particular of children, be processed; or where processing 

involves a large amount of personal data and affect a large number of data subjects. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 47 
DGD 2 EN 


(76) The likelihood and severity of the risk to the right and freedom of the data subject should 

be determine by reference to the nature, scope, context and purpose of the processing. 

Risk should be evaluate on the basis of an objective assessment, by which it be establish 

whether data processing operation involve a risk or a high risk. 

(77) Guidance on the implementation of appropriate measure and on the demonstration of 

compliance by the controller or the processor, especially a regard the identification of the 

risk related to the processing, their assessment in term of origin, nature, likelihood and 

severity, and the identification of best practice to mitigate the risk, could be provide in 

particular by mean of approve code of conduct, approve certifications, guideline 

provide by the Board or indication provide by a data protection officer. The Board may 

also issue guideline on processing operation that be consider to be unlikely to result in 

a high risk to the right and freedom of natural person and indicate what measure may 

be sufficient in such case to address such risk. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 48 
DGD 2 EN 


(78) The protection of the right and freedom of natural person with regard to the processing 

of personal data require that appropriate technical and organisational measure be take to 

ensure that the requirement of this Regulation be met. In order to be able to demonstrate 

compliance with this Regulation, the controller should adopt internal policy and 

implement measure which meet in particular the principle of data protection by design 

and data protection by default. Such measure could consist, inter alia, of minimise the 

processing of personal data, pseudonymising personal data a soon a possible, 

transparency with regard to the function and processing of personal data, enable the data 

subject to monitor the data processing, enable the controller to create and improve 

security features. When developing, designing, select and use applications, service 

and product that be base on the processing of personal data or process personal data to 

fulfil their task, producer of the products, service and application should be encourage 

to take into account the right to data protection when develop and design such 

products, service and application and, with due regard to the state of the art, to make sure 

that controller and processor be able to fulfil their data protection obligations.The 

principle of data protection by design and by default should also be take into 

consideration in the context of public tenders. 

(79) The protection of the right and freedom of data subject a well a the responsibility and 

liability of controller and processors, also in relation to the monitoring by and measure of 

supervisory authorities, require a clear allocation of the responsibility under this 

Regulation, include where a controller determines the purpose and mean of the 

processing jointly with other controller or where a processing operation be carry out on 

behalf of a controller. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 49 
DGD 2 EN 


(80) Where a controller or a processor not establish in the Union be processing personal data 

of data subject who be in the Union whose processing activity be related to the offering 

of good or services, irrespective of whether a payment of the data subject be required, to 

such data subject in the Union, or to the monitoring of their behaviour a far a their 

behaviour take place within the Union, the controller or the processor should designate a 

representative, unless the processing be occasional, do not include processing, on a large 

scale, of special category of personal data or the processing of personal data relate to 

criminal conviction and offences, and be unlikely to result in a risk to the right and 

freedom of natural persons, take into account the nature, context, scope and purpose of 

the processing or if the controller be a public authority or body. The representative should 

act on behalf of the controller or the processor and may be address by any supervisory 

authority. The representative should be explicitly designate by a write mandate of the 

controller or the processor to act on it behalf with regard to their obligation under this 

Regulation. The designation of such representative do not affect the responsibility and 

liability of the controller or the processor under this Regulation. Such representative should 

perform it task accord to the mandate receive from the controller or processor, 

include to cooperate with the competent supervisory authority on any action take in 

ensure compliance with this Regulation. The designate representative should be subject 

to enforcement proceeding in the event of non-compliance by the controller or processor. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 50 
DGD 2 EN 


(81) To ensure compliance with the requirement of this Regulation in respect of the processing 

to be carry out by the processor on behalf of the controller, when entrust a processor 

with processing activities, the controller should use only processor provide sufficient 

guarantees, in particular in term of expert knowledge, reliability and resources, to 

implement technical and organisational measure which will meet the requirement of this 

Regulation, include for the security of processing. The adherence of the processor to an 

approve code of conduct or an approve certification mechanism may be use a an 

element to demonstrate compliance with the obligation of the controller. The carrying-out 

of processing by a processor should be govern by a contract or other legal act under 

Union or Member State law, binding the processor to the controller, set out the 

subject-matter and duration of the processing, the nature and purpose of the processing, 

the type of personal data and category of data subjects, take into account the specific 

task and responsibility of the processor in the context of the processing to be carry out 

and the risk to the right and freedom of the data subject. The controller and processor 

may choose to use an individual contract or standard contractual clause which be adopt 

either directly by the Commission or by a supervisory authority in accordance with the 

consistency mechanism and then adopt by the Commission. After the completion of the 

processing on behalf of the controller, the processor should, at the choice of the controller,
