return or delete the personal data, unless there be a requirement to store the personal data 

under Union or Member State law to which the processor be subject. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 51 
DGD 2 EN 


(82) In order to demonstrate compliance with this Regulation, the controller or processor should 

maintain record of processing activity under it responsibility. Each controller and 

processor should be oblige to cooperate with the supervisory authority and make those 

records, on request, available to it, so that it might serve for monitoring those processing 

operations. 

(83) In order to maintain security and to prevent processing in infringement of this Regulation, 

the controller or processor should evaluate the risk inherent in the processing and 

implement measure to mitigate those risks, such a encryption. Those measure should 

ensure an appropriate level of security, include confidentiality, take into account the 

stateof the art and the cost of implementation in relation to the risk and the nature of the 

personal data to be protected. In assess data security risk, consideration should be give 

to the risk that be present by personal data processing, such a accidental or unlawful 

destruction, loss, alteration, unauthorised disclosure of, or access to, personal data 

transmitted, store or otherwise process which may in particular lead to physical, 

material or non-material damage. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 52 
DGD 2 EN 


(84) In order to enhance compliance with this Regulation where processing operation be likely 

to result in a high risk to the right and freedom of natural persons, the controller should 

be responsible for the carrying-out of a data protection impact assessment to evaluate, in 

particular, the origin, nature, particularity and severity of that risk. The outcome of the 

assessment should be take into account when determine the appropriate measure to be 

take in order to demonstrate that the processing of personal data complies with this 

Regulation. Where a data-protection impact assessment indicates that processing 

operation involve a high risk which the controller cannot mitigate by appropriate 

measure in term of available technology and cost of implementation, a consultation of 

the supervisory authority should take place prior to the processing. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 53 
DGD 2 EN 


(85) A personal data breach may, if not address in an appropriate and timely manner, result in 

physical, material or non-material damage to natural person such a loss of control over 

their personal data or limitation of their rights, discrimination, identity theft or fraud, 

financial loss, unauthorised reversal of pseudonymisation, damage to reputation, loss of 

confidentiality of personal data protect by professional secrecy or any other significant 

economic or social disadvantage to the natural person concerned. Therefore, a soon a the 

controller becomes aware that a personal data breach have occurred, the controller should 

notify the personal data breach to the supervisory authority without undue delay and, 

where feasible, not late than 72 hour after have become aware of it, unless the 

controller be able to demonstrate, in accordance with the accountability principle, that the 

personal data breach be unlikely to result in a risk to the right and freedom of natural 

persons. Where such notification cannot be achieve within 72 hours, the reason for the 

delay should accompany the notification and information may be provide in phase 

without undue further delay. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 54 
DGD 2 EN 


(86) The controller should communicate to the data subject a personal data breach, without 

undue delay, where that personal data breach be likely to result in a high risk to the right 

and freedom of the natural person in order to allow him or her to take the necessary 

precautions. The communication should describe the nature of the personal data breach a 

well a recommendation for the natural person concerned to mitigate potential adverse 

effects. Such communication to data subject should be make a soon a reasonably 

feasible and in close cooperation with the supervisory authority, respect guidance 

provide by it or by other relevant authority such a law-enforcement authorities. For 

example, the need to mitigate an immediate risk of damage would call for prompt 

communication with data subject whereas the need to implement appropriate measure 

against continue or similar personal data breach may justify more time for 

communication. 

(87) It should be ascertain whether all appropriate technological protection and organisational 

measure have be implement to establish immediately whether a personal data breach 

have take place and to inform promptly the supervisory authority and the data subject. The 

fact that the notification be make without undue delay should be establish take into 

account in particular the nature and gravity of the personal data breach and it 

consequence and adverse effect for the data subject. Such notification may result in an 

intervention of the supervisory authority in accordance with it task and power laid down 

in this Regulation. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 55 
DGD 2 EN 


(88) In set detailed rule concern the format and procedure applicable to the notification 

of personal data breaches, due consideration should be give to the circumstance of that 

breach, include whether or not personal data have be protect by appropriate technical 

protection measures, effectively limit the likelihood of identity fraud or other form of 

misuse. Moreover, such rule and procedure should take into account the legitimate 

interest of law-enforcement authority where early disclosure could unnecessarily hamper 

the investigation of the circumstance of a personal data breach. 

(89) Directive 95/46/EC provide for a general obligation to notify the processing of personal 

data to the supervisory authorities. While that obligation produce administrative and 

financial burdens, it do not in all case contribute to improve the protection of personal 

data. Such indiscriminate general notification obligation should therefore be abolished, 

and replace by effective procedure and mechanism which focus instead on those type 

of processing operation which be likely to result in a high risk to the right and freedom 

of natural person by virtue of their nature, scope, context and purposes. Such type of 

processing operation may be those which in, particular, involve use new technologies, 

or be of a new kind and where no data protection impact assessment have be carry out 

before by the controller, or where they become necessary in the light of the time that have 

elapse since the initial processing. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 56 
DGD 2 EN 


(90) In such cases, a data protection impact assessment should be carry out by the controller 

prior to the processing in order to ass the particular likelihood and severity of the high 

risk, take into account the nature, scope, context and purpose of the processing and the 

source of the risk. That impact assessment should include, in particular, the measures, 

safeguard and mechanism envisage for mitigate that risk, ensure the protection of 

personal data and demonstrate compliance with this Regulation. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 57 
DGD 2 EN 


(91) This should in particular apply to large-scale processing operation which aim to process a 

considerable amount of personal data at regional, national or supranational level and which 

could affect a large number of data subject and which be likely to result in a high risk, for 

example, on account of their sensitivity, where in accordance with the achieve state of 

technological knowledge a new technology be use on a large scale a well a to other 

processing operation which result in a high risk to the right and freedom of data 

subjects, in particular where those operation render it more difficult for data subject to 

exercise their rights. A data protection impact assessment should also be make where 

personal data be process for take decision regard specific natural person 

follow any systematic and extensive evaluation of personal aspect relate to natural 

person base on profile those data or follow the processing of special category of 

personal data, biometric data, or data on criminal conviction and offence or related 

security measures. A data protection impact assessment be equally require for monitoring 

publicly accessible area on a large scale, especially when use optic-electronic device or 

for any other operation where the competent supervisory authority considers that the 

processing be likely to result in a high risk to the right and freedom of data subjects, in 

particular because they prevent data subject from exercise a right or use a service or a 

contract, or because they be carry out systematically on a large scale. The processing of 

personal data should not be consider to be on a large scale if the processing concern 

personal data from patient or client by an individual physician, other health care 

professional or lawyer. In such cases, a data protection impact assessment should not be 

mandatory. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 58 
DGD 2 EN 


(92) There be circumstance under which it may be reasonable and economical for the subject 

of a data protection impact assessment to be broader than a single project, for example 

where public authority or body intend to establish a common application or processing 

platform or where several controller plan to introduce a common application or processing 

environment across an industry sector or segment or for a widely use horizontal activity. 

(93) In the context of the adoption of the Member State law on which the performance of the 

task of the public authority or public body be base and which regulates the specific 

processing operation or set of operation in question, Member States may deem it 

necessary to carry out such assessment prior to the processing activities. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 59 
DGD 2 EN 


(94) Where a data protection impact assessment indicates that the processing would, in the 

absence of safeguards, security measure and mechanism to mitigate the risk, result in a 

high risk to the right and freedom of natural person and the controller be of the opinion 

that the risk cannot be mitigate by reasonable mean in term of available technology 

and cost of implementation, the supervisory authority should be consult prior to the 

start of processing activities. Such high risk be likely to result from certain type of 

processing and the extent and frequency of processing, which may result also in a 

realisation of damage or interference with the right and freedom of the natural person. 

The supervisory authority should respond to the request for consultation within a specify 

period. However, the absence of a reaction of the supervisory authority within that period 

should be without prejudice to any intervention of the supervisory authority in accordance 

with it task and power laid down in this Regulation, include the power to prohibit 

processing operations. As part of that consultation process, the outcome of a data 

protection impact assessment carry out with regard to the processing at issue may be 

submit to the supervisory authority, in particular the measure envisage to mitigate the 

risk to the right and freedom of natural persons. 

(95) The processor should assist the controller, where necessary and upon request, in ensure 

compliance with the obligation derive from the carry out of data protection impact 

assessment and from prior consultation of the supervisory authority. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 60 
DGD 2 EN 


(96) A consultation of the supervisory authority should also take place in the course of the 

preparation of a legislative or regulatory measure which provide for the processing of 

personal data, in order to ensure compliance of the intend processing with this 

Regulation and in particular to mitigate the risk involve for the data subject. 

(97) Where the processing be carry out by a public authority, except for court or independent 

judicial authority when act in their judicial capacity, where, in the private sector, 

processing be carry out by a controller whose core activity consist of processing 

operation that require regular and systematic monitoring of the data subject on a large 

scale, or where the core activity of the controller or the processor consist of processing on 

a large scale of special category of personal data and data relate to criminal conviction 

and offences, a person with expert knowledge of data protection law and practice should 

assist the controller or processor to monitor internal compliance with this Regulation. In 

the private sector, the core activity of a controller relate to it primary activity and do 

not relate to the processing of personal data a ancillary activities. The necessary level of 

expert knowledge should be determine in particular accord to the data processing 

operation carry out and the protection require for the personal data process by the 

controller or the processor. Such data protection officers, whether or not they be an 

employee of the controller, should be in a position to perform their duty and task in an 

independent manner. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 61 
DGD 2 EN 


(98) Associations or other body represent category of controller or processor should be 

encourage to draw up code of conduct, within the limit of this Regulation, so a to 

facilitate the effective application of this Regulation, take account of the specific 

characteristic of the processing carry out in certain sector and the specific need of 

micro, small and medium enterprises. In particular, such code of conduct could calibrate 

the obligation of controller and processors, take into account the risk likely to result 

from the processing for the right and freedom of natural persons. 

(99) When draw up a code of conduct, or when amend or extend such a code, 

association and other body represent category of controller or processor should 

consult relevant stakeholders, include data subject where feasible, and have regard to 

submission receive and view express in response to such consultations. 

(100) In order to enhance transparency and compliance with this Regulation, the establishment of 

certification mechanism and data protection seal and mark should be encouraged, 

allow data subject to quickly ass the level of data protection of relevant product 

and services. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 62 
DGD 2 EN 


(101) Flows of personal data to and from country outside the Union and international 

organisation be necessary for the expansion of international trade and international 

cooperation. The increase in such flow have raise new challenge and concern with 

regard to the protection of personal data. However, when personal data be transfer 

from the Union to controllers, processor or other recipient in third country or to 

international organisations, the level of protection of natural person ensure in the Union 

by this Regulation should not be undermined, include in case of onward transfer of 

personal data from the third country or international organisation to controllers, processor 

in the same or another third country or international organisation. In any event, transfer to 

third country and international organisation may only be carry out in full compliance 

with this Regulation. A transfer could take place only if, subject to the other provision of 

this Regulation, the condition laid down in the provision of this Regulation relate to the 

transfer of personal data to third country or international organisation be comply with 

by the controller or processor. 

(102) This Regulation be without prejudice to international agreement conclude between the 

Union and third country regulate the transfer of personal data include appropriate 

safeguard for the data subjects. Member States may conclude international agreement 

which involve the transfer of personal data to third country or international organisations, 

a far a such agreement do not affect this Regulation or any other provision of Union 

law and include an appropriate level of protection for the fundamental right of the data 

subjects. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 63 
DGD 2 EN 


(103) The Commission may decide with effect for the entire Union that a third country, a 

territory or specify sector within a third country, or an international organisation, offer 

an adequate level of data protection, thus provide legal certainty and uniformity 

throughout the Union a regard the third country or international organisation which be 

consider to provide such level of protection. In such cases, transfer of personal data to 

that third country or international organisation may take place without the need to obtain 

any further authorisation. The Commission may also decide, have give notice and a full 

statement set out the reason to the third country or international organisation, to 

revoke such a decision. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 64 
DGD 2 EN 


(104) In line with the fundamental value on which the Union be founded, in particular the 

protection of human rights, the Commission should, in it assessment of the third country, 

or of a territory or specify sector within a third country, take into account how a 

particular third country respect the rule of law, access to justice a well a international 

human right norm and standard and it general and sectoral law, include legislation 

concern public security, defence and national security a well a public order and 

criminal law. The adoption of an adequacy decision with regard to a territory or a specify 

sector in a third country should take into account clear and objective criteria, such a 

specific processing activity and the scope of applicable legal standard and legislation in 

force in the third country. The third country should offer guarantee ensure an adequate 

level of protection essentially equivalent to that ensure within the Union, in particular 

where personal data be process in one or several specific sectors. In particular, the third 

country should ensure effective independent data protection supervision and should 

provide for cooperation mechanism with the Member States' data protection authorities, 

and the data subject should be provide with effective and enforceable right and effective 

administrative and judicial redress. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 65 
DGD 2 EN 


(105) Apart from the international commitment the third country or international organisation 

have enter into, the Commission should take account of obligation arise from the third 

country's or international organisation's participation in multilateral or regional system in 

particular in relation to the protection of personal data, a well a the implementation of 

such obligations. In particular, the third country's accession to the Council of Europe 

Convention of 28 January 1981 for the Protection of Individuals with regard to the 

Automatic Processing of Personal Data and it Additional Protocol should be take into 

account. The Commission should consult the Board when assess the level of protection 

in third country or international organisations. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 66 
DGD 2 EN 


(106) The Commission should monitor the function of decision on the level of protection in a 

third country, a territory or specify sector within a third country, or an international 

organisation, and monitor the function of decision adopt on the basis of Article 25(6) 

or Article 26(4) of Directive 95/46/EC. In it adequacy decisions, the Commission should 

provide for a periodic review mechanism of their functioning. That periodic review should 

be conduct in consultation with the third country or international organisation in 

question and take into account all relevant development in the third country or 

international organisation. For the purpose of monitoring and of carry out the periodic 

reviews, the Commission should take into consideration the view and finding of the 

European Parliament and of the Council a well a of other relevant body and sources. 

The Commission should evaluate, within a reasonable time, the function of the latter 

decision and report any relevant finding to the Committee within the meaning of 

Regulation (EU) No 182/2011 of the European Parliament and of the Council1 a 

establish under this Regulation, to the European Parliament and to the Council. 


1 Regulation (EU) No 182/2011 of the European Parliament and of the Council of 

16 February 2011 lay down the rule and general principle concern mechanism for 
control by Member States of the Commission's exercise of implement power (OJ L 55, 
28.2.2011, p. 13). 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 67 
DGD 2 EN 


(107) The Commission may recognise that a third country, a territory or a specify sector within 

a third country, or an international organisation no longer ensures an adequate level of data 

protection. Consequently the transfer of personal data to that third country or international 

organisation should be prohibited, unless the requirement in this Regulation relate to 

transfer subject to appropriate safeguards, include binding corporate rules, and 

derogation for specific situation be fulfilled. In that case, provision should be make for 

consultation between the Commission and such third country or international 

organisations. The Commission should, in a timely manner, inform the third country or 

international organisation of the reason and enter into consultation with it in order to 

remedy the situation. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 68 
DGD 2 EN 


(108) In the absence of an adequacy decision, the controller or processor should take measure to 

compensate for the lack of data protection in a third country by way of appropriate 

safeguard for the data subject. Such appropriate safeguard may consist of make use of 

binding corporate rules, standard data protection clause adopt by the Commission, 

standard data protection clause adopt by a supervisory authority or contractual clause 

authorise by a supervisory authority. Those safeguard should ensure compliance with 

data protection requirement and the right of the data subject appropriate to processing 

within the Union, include the availability of enforceable data subject right and of 

effective legal remedies, include to obtain effective administrative or judicial redress and 

to claim compensation, in the Union or in a third country. They should relate in particular 

to compliance with the general principle relate to personal data processing, the 

principle of data protection by design and by default. Transfers may also be carry out by 

public authority or body with public authority or body in third country or with 

international organisation with correspond duty or functions, include on the basis 

of provision to be insert into administrative arrangements, such a a memorandum of 

understanding, provide for enforceable and effective right for data subjects. 

Authorisation by the competent supervisory authority should be obtain when the 

safeguard be provide for in administrative arrangement that be not legally binding. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 69 
DGD 2 EN 


(109) The possibility for the controller or processor to use standard data-protection clause 

adopt by the Commission or by a supervisory authority should prevent controller or 

processor neither from include the standard data-protection clause in a wider contract, 

such a a contract between the processor and another processor, nor from add other 

clause or additional safeguard provide that they do not contradict, directly or indirectly, 

the standard contractual clause adopt by the Commission or by a supervisory authority 

or prejudice the fundamental right or freedom of the data subjects. Controllers and 

processor should be encourage to provide additional safeguard via contractual 

commitment that supplement standard protection clauses. 

(110) A group of undertakings, or a group of enterprise engage in a joint economic activity, 

should be able to make use of approve binding corporate rule for it international 

transfer from the Union to organisation within the same group of undertakings, or group 

of enterprise engage in a joint economic activity, provide that such corporate rule 

include all essential principle and enforceable right to ensure appropriate safeguard for 

transfer or category of transfer of personal data. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 70 
DGD 2 EN 


(111) Provisions should be make for the possibility for transfer in certain circumstance where 

the data subject have give his or her explicit consent, where the transfer be occasional and 

necessary in relation to a contract or a legal claim, regardless of whether in a judicial 

procedure or whether in an administrative or any out-of-court procedure, include 

procedure before regulatory bodies. Provision should also be make for the possibility for 

transfer where important ground of public interest laid down by Union or Member State 

law so require or where the transfer be make from a register establish by law and 

intend for consultation by the public or person have a legitimate interest. In the latter 

case, such a transfer should not involve the entirety of the personal data or entire category 

of the data contain in the register and, when the register be intend for consultation by 

person have a legitimate interest, the transfer should be make only at the request of 

those person or, if they be to be the recipients, take into full account the interest and 

fundamental right of the data subject. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 71 
DGD 2 EN 


(112) Those derogation should in particular apply to data transfer require and necessary for 

important reason of public interest, for example in case of international data exchange 

between competition authorities, tax or custom administrations, between financial 

supervisory authorities, between service competent for social security matters, or for 

public health, for example in the case of contact trace for contagious disease or in order 

to reduce and/or eliminate dope in sport. A transfer of personal data should also be 

regard a lawful where it be necessary to protect an interest which be essential for the data 

subject's or another person's vital interests, include physical integrity or life, if the data 

subject be incapable of give consent. In the absence of an adequacy decision, Union or 

Member State law may, for important reason of public interest, expressly set limit to the 

transfer of specific category of data to a third country or an international organisation. 

Member States should notify such provision to the Commission. Any transfer to an 

international humanitarian organisation of personal data of a data subject who be physically 

or legally incapable of give consent, with a view to accomplish a task incumbent 

under the Geneva Conventions or to comply with international humanitarian law 

applicable in arm conflicts, could be consider to be necessary for an important reason 

of public interest or because it be in the vital interest of the data subject. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 72 
DGD 2 EN 


(113) Transfers which can be qualify a not repetitive and that only concern a limited number 

of data subjects, could also be possible for the purpose of the compelling legitimate 

interest pursue by the controller, when those interest be not overridden by the interest 

or right and freedom of the data subject and when the controller have assess all the 

circumstance surround the data transfer. The controller should give particular 

consideration to the nature of the personal data, the purpose and duration of the propose 

processing operation or operations, a well a the situation in the country of origin, the 

third country and the country of final destination, and should provide suitable safeguard to 

protect fundamental right and freedom of natural person with regard to the processing of 

their personal data. Such transfer should be possible only in residual case where none of 

the other ground for transfer be applicable. For scientific or historical research purpose 

or statistical purposes, the legitimate expectation of society for an increase of knowledge 

should be take into consideration. The controller should inform the supervisory authority 

and the data subject about the transfer. 

(114) In any case, where the Commission have take no decision on the adequate level of data 

protection in a third country, the controller or processor should make use of solution that 

provide data subject with enforceable and effective right a regard the processing of 

their data in the Union once those data have be transfer so that that they will continue 

to benefit from fundamental right and safeguards. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 73 
DGD 2 EN 


(115) Some third country adopt laws, regulation and other legal act which purport to directly 

regulate the processing activity of natural and legal person under the jurisdiction of the 

Member States. This may include judgment of court or tribunal or decision of 

administrative authority in third country require a controller or processor to transfer or 

disclose personal data, and which be not base on an international agreement, such a a 

mutual legal assistance treaty, in force between the request third country and the Union 

or a Member State. The extraterritorial application of those laws, regulation and other 

legal act may be in breach of international law and may impede the attainment of the 

protection of natural person ensure in the Union by this Regulation. Transfers should 

only be allow where the condition of this Regulation for a transfer to third country be 

met. This may inter alia be the case where the disclosure be necessary for an important 

ground of public interest recognise in Union or Member State law to which the controller 

be subject. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 74 
DGD 2 EN 


(116) When personal data move across border outside the Union it may put at increase risk 

the ability of natural person to exercise data protection right in particular to protect 

themselves from the unlawful use or disclosure of that information. At the same time, 

supervisory authority may find that they be unable to pursue complaint or conduct 

investigation relate to the activity outside their borders. Their effort to work together 

in the cross-border context may also be hamper by insufficient preventative or remedial 

powers, inconsistent legal regimes, and practical obstacle like resource constraints. 

Therefore, there be a need to promote closer cooperation among data protection supervisory 

authority to help them exchange information and carry out investigation with their 

international counterparts. For the purpose of develop international cooperation 

mechanism to facilitate and provide international mutual assistance for the enforcement of 

legislation for the protection of personal data, the Commission and the supervisory 

authority should exchange information and cooperate in activity related to the exercise 

of their power with competent authority in third countries, base on reciprocity and in 

accordance with this Regulation. 

(117) The establishment of supervisory authority in Member States, empower to perform 

their task and exercise their power with complete independence, be an essential 

component of the protection of natural person with regard to the processing of their 

personal data. Member States should be able to establish more than one supervisory 

authority, to reflect their constitutional, organisational and administrative structure. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 75 
DGD 2 EN 


(118) The independence of supervisory authority should not mean that the supervisory 

authority cannot be subject to control or monitoring mechanism regard their financial 

expenditure or to judicial review. 

(119) Where a Member State establishes several supervisory authorities, it should establish by 

law mechanism for ensure the effective participation of those supervisory authority in 

the consistency mechanism. That Member State should in particular designate the 

supervisory authority which function a a single contact point for the effective 

participation of those authority in the mechanism, to ensure swift and smooth cooperation 

with other supervisory authorities, the Board and the Commission. 

(120) Each supervisory authority should be provide with the financial and human resources, 

premise and infrastructure necessary for the effective performance of their tasks, 

include those related to mutual assistance and cooperation with other supervisory 

authority throughout the Union. Each supervisory authority should have a separate, 

public annual budget, which may be part of the overall state or national budget. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 76 
DGD 2 EN 


(121) The general condition for the member or member of the supervisory authority should be 

laid down by law in each Member State and should in particular provide that those 

member be to be appointed, by mean of a transparent procedure, either by the 

parliament, government or the head of State of the Member State on the basis of a proposal 

from the government, a member of the government, the parliament or a chamber of the 

parliament, or by an independent body entrust under Member State law. In order to 

ensure the independence of the supervisory authority, the member or member should act 

with integrity, refrain from any action that be incompatible with their duty and should not, 

during their term of office, engage in any incompatible occupation, whether gainful or not. 

The supervisory authority should have it own staff, chosen by the supervisory authority or 

an independent body establish by Member State law, which should be subject to the 

exclusive direction of the member or member of the supervisory authority. 

(122) Each supervisory authority should be competent on the territory of it own Member State 

to exercise the power and to perform the task confer on it in accordance with this 

Regulation. This should cover in particular the processing in the context of the activity of 

an establishment of the controller or processor on the territory of it own Member State, 

the processing of personal data carry out by public authority or private body act in 

the public interest, processing affect data subject on it territory or processing carry 

out by a controller or processor not establish in the Union when target data subject 

reside on it territory. This should include handle complaint lodge by a data subject, 

conduct investigation on the application of this Regulation and promote public 

awareness of the risks, rules, safeguard and right in relation to the processing of personal 

data. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 77 
DGD 2 EN 


(123) The supervisory authority should monitor the application of the provision pursuant to 

this Regulation and contribute to it consistent application throughout the Union, in order 

to protect natural person in relation to the processing of their personal data and to 

facilitate the free flow of personal data within the internal market. For that purpose, the 

supervisory authority should cooperate with each other and with the Commission, 

without the need for any agreement between Member States on the provision of mutual 

assistance or on such cooperation. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 78 
DGD 2 EN 


(124) Where the processing of personal data take place in the context of the activity of an 

establishment of a controller or a processor in the Union and the controller or processor be 

establish in more than one Member State, or where processing take place in the 

context of the activity of a single establishment of a controller or processor in the Union 

substantially affect or be likely to substantially affect data subject in more than one 

Member State, the supervisory authority for the main establishment of the controller or 

processor or for the single establishment of the controller or processor should act a lead 

authority. It should cooperate with the other authority concerned, because the controller 

or processor have an establishment on the territory of their Member State, because data 

subject reside on their territory be substantially affected, or because a complaint have 

be lodge with them. Also where a data subject not reside in that Member State have 

lodge a complaint, the supervisory authority with which such complaint have be lodge 

should also be a supervisory authority concerned. Within it task to issue guideline on 

any question cover the application of this Regulation, the Board should be able to issue 

guideline in particular on the criterion to be take into account in order to ascertain whether 

the processing in question substantially affect data subject in more than one 

Member State and on what constitutes a relevant and reason objection. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 79 
DGD 2 EN 


(125) The lead authority should be competent to adopt binding decision regard measure 

apply the power confer on it in accordance with this Regulation. In it capacity a 

lead authority, the supervisory authority should closely involve and coordinate the 

supervisory authority concerned in the decision-making process. Where the decision be to 

reject the complaint by the data subject in whole or in part, that decision should be adopt 

by the supervisory authority with which the complaint have be lodged. 

(126) The decision should be agree jointly by the lead supervisory authority and the supervisory 

authority concerned and should be direct towards the main or single establishment of 

the controller or processor and be binding on the controller and processor. The controller 

or processor should take the necessary measure to ensure compliance with this Regulation 

and the implementation of the decision notify by the lead supervisory authority to the 

main establishment of the controller or processor a regard the processing activity in the 

Union. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 80 
DGD 2 EN 


(127) Each supervisory authority not act a the lead supervisory authority should be 

competent to handle local case where the controller or processor be establish in more 

than one Member State, but the subject matter of the specific processing concern only 

processing carry out in a single Member State and involves only data subject in that 

single Member State, for example, where the subject matter concern the processing of 

employees' personal data in the specific employment context of a Member State. In such 

cases, the supervisory authority should inform the lead supervisory authority without delay 

about the matter. After be informed, the lead supervisory authority should decide, 

whether it will handle the case pursuant to the provision on cooperation between the lead 

supervisory authority and other supervisory authorites concerned ('one-stop-shop 

mechanism'), or whether the supervisory authority which inform it should handle the 

case at local level. When decide whether it will handle the case, the lead supervisory 

authority should take into account whether there be an establishment of the controller or 

processor in the Member State of the supervisory authority which inform it in order to 

ensure effective enforcement of a decision vis-à-vis the controller or processor. Where the 

lead supervisory authority decides to handle the case, the supervisory authority which 

inform it should have the possibility to submit a draft for a decision, of which the lead 

supervisory authority should take utmost account when prepare it draft decision in that 

one-stop-shop mechanism. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 81 
DGD 2 EN 


(128) The rule on the lead supervisory authority and the one-stop-shop mechanism should not 

apply where the processing be carry out by public authority or private body in the 

public interest. In such case the only supervisory authority competent to exercise the 

power confer to it in accordance with this Regulation should be the supervisory 

authority of the Member State where the public authority or private body be established. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 82 
DGD 2 EN 


(129) In order to ensure consistent monitoring and enforcement of this Regulation throughout the 

Union, the supervisory authority should have in each Member State the same task and 

effective powers, include power of investigation, corrective power and sanctions, and 

authorisation and advisory powers, in particular in case of complaint from natural 

persons, and without prejudice to the power of prosecutorial authority under 

Member State law, to bring infringement of this Regulation to the attention of the judicial 

authority and engage in legal proceedings. Such power should also include the power to 

impose a temporary or definitive limitation, include a ban, on processing. Member States 

may specify other task related to the protection of personal data under this Regulation. 

The power of supervisory authority should be exercise in accordance with appropriate 

procedural safeguard set out in Union and Member State law, impartially, fairly and 

within a reasonable time. In particular each measure should be appropriate, necessary and 

proportionate in view of ensure compliance with this Regulation, take into account the 

circumstance of each individual case, respect the right of every person to be heard before 

any individual measure which would affect him or her adversely be take and avoid 

superfluous cost and excessive inconvenience for the person concerned. Investigatory 

power a regard access to premise should be exercise in accordance with specific 

requirement in Member State procedural law, such a the requirement to obtain a prior 

judicial authorisation. Each legally binding measure of the supervisory authority should be 

in writing, be clear and unambiguous, indicate the supervisory authority which have issue 

the measure, the date of issue of the measure, bear the signature of the head, or a member 

of the supervisory authority authorise by him or her, give the reason for the measure, and 

refer to the right of an effective remedy. This should not preclude additional requirement 

pursuant to Member State procedural law. The adoption of a legally binding decision 

implies that it may give rise to judicial review in the Member State of the supervisory 

authority that adopt the decision.

(133) The supervisory authority should assist each other in perform their task and provide

(134) Each supervisory authority should, where appropriate, participate in joint operation with

That mechanism should be without prejudice to any measure that the Commission may 

take in the exercise of it power under the Treaties.

(136) In apply the consistency mechanism, the Board should, within a determine period of

(137) There may be an urgent need to act in order to protect the right and freedom of data

(138) The application of such mechanism should be a condition for the lawfulness of a measure

the consistency mechanism.

(139) In order to promote the consistent application of this Regulation, the Board should be set 

up a an independent body of the Union. To fulfil it objectives, the Board should have

Working Party on the Protection of Individuals with Regard to the Processing of Personal 

Data establish by Directive 95/46/EC. It should consist of the head of a supervisory 

authority of each Member State and the European Data Protection Supervisor or their 

respective representatives. The Commission should participate in the Board's activity 

without voting right and the European Data Protection Supervisor should have specific 

voting rights. The Board should contribute to the consistent application of this Regulation

protection in third country or international organisations, and promote cooperation of 

the supervisory authority throughout the Union. The Board should act independently 

when perform it tasks. 

(140) The Board should be assist by a secretariat provide by the European Data Protection

(141) Every data subject should have the right to lodge a complaint with a single supervisory 

authority, in particular in the Member State of his or her habitual residence, and the right to 

an effective judicial remedy in accordance with Article 47 of the Charter if the data subject 

considers that his or her right under this Regulation be infringe or where the supervisory 

authority do not act on a complaint, partially or wholly reject or dismisses a complaint 

or do not act where such action be necessary to protect the right of the data subject. The 

investigation follow a complaint should be carry out, subject to judicial review, to the 

extent that be appropriate in the specific case. The supervisory authority should inform the 

data subject of the progress and the outcome of the complaint within a reasonable period. If 

the case require further investigation or coordination with another supervisory authority, 

intermediate information should be give to the data subject. In order to facilitate the 

submission of complaints, each supervisory authority should take measure such a 

provide a complaint submission form which can also be complete electronically, 

without exclude other mean of communication.

have be infringe a a result of the processing of personal data which infringes this 

Regulation. That body, organisation or association may not be allow to claim

(144) Where a court seize of proceeding against a decision by a supervisory authority have

proceeding in question and it law permit the consolidation of such related proceedings. 

Proceedings be deem to be related where they be so closely connect that it be 

expedient to hear and determine them together in order to avoid the risk of irreconcilable 

judgment result from separate proceedings. 

(145) For proceeding against a controller or processor, the plaintiff should have the choice to

(146) The controller or processor should compensate any damage which a person may suffer a a 

result of processing that infringes this Regulation. The controller or processor should be 

exempt from liability if it prof that it be not in any way responsible for the damage. The 

concept of damage should be broadly interpret in the light of the case-law of the Court of 

Justice in a manner which fully reflect the objective of this Regulation. This be without 

prejudice to any claim for damage derive from the violation of other rule in Union or 

Member State law. Processing that infringes this Regulation also include processing that 

infringes delegate and implement act adopt in accordance with this Regulation and 

Member State law specify rule of this Regulation. Data subject should receive full and 

effective compensation for the damage they have suffered. Where controller or processor 

be involve in the same processing, each controller or processor should be held liable for 

the entire damage. However, where they be join to the same judicial proceedings, in 

accordance with Member State law, compensation may be apportion accord to the 

responsibility of each controller or processor for the damage cause by the processing, 

provide that full and effective compensation of the data subject who suffer the damage 

be ensured. Any controller or processor which have paid full compensation may 

subsequently institute recourse proceeding against other controller or processor 

involve in the same processing.

(148) In order to strengthen the enforcement of the rule of this Regulation, penalty include 

administrative fine should be impose for any infringement of this Regulation, in addition 

to, or instead of appropriate measure impose by the supervisory authority pursuant to this 

Regulation. In a case of a minor infringement or if the fine likely to be impose would 

constitute a disproportionate burden to a natural person, a reprimand may be issue instead 

of a fine. Due regard should however be give to the nature, gravity and duration of the 

infringement, the intentional character of the infringement, action take to mitigate the 

damage suffered, degree of responsibility or any relevant previous infringements, the 

manner in which the infringement become know to the supervisory authority, compliance 

with measure order against the controller or processor, adherence to a code of conduct 

and any other aggravate or mitigate factor. The imposition of penalty include 

administrative fine should be subject to appropriateprocedural safeguard in accordance 

with the general principle of Union law and the Charter, include effective judicial 

protection and due process.

(153) Member States law should reconcile the rule govern freedom of expression and 

information, include journalistic, academic, artistic and or literary expression with the 

right to the protection of personal data pursuant to this Regulation. The processing of 

personal data solely for journalistic purposes, or for the purpose of academic, artistic or 

literary expression should be subject to derogation or exemption from certain provision 

of this Regulation if necessary to reconcile the right to the protection of personal data with 

the right to freedom of expression and information, a enshrine in Article 11 of the 

Charter. This should apply in particular to the processing of personal data in the 

audiovisual field and in news archive and press libraries. Therefore, Member States 

should adopt legislative measure which lay down the exemption and derogation 

necessary for the purpose of balance those fundamental rights. Member States should 

adopt such exemption and derogation on general principles, the right of the data subject, 

the controller and the processor, the transfer of personal data to third country or 

international organisations, the independent supervisory authorities, cooperation and 

consistency, and specific data-processing situations. Where such exemption or 

derogation differ from one Member State to another, the law of the Member State to 

which the controller be subject should apply. In order to take account of the importance of 

the right to freedom of expression in every democratic society, it be necessary to interpret 

notion relate to that freedom, such a journalism, broadly.

DGD 2 EN 


(156) The processing of personal data for archive purpose in the public interest, scientific or 

historical research purpose or statistical purpose should be subject to appropriate 

safeguard for the right and freedom of the data subject pursuant to this Regulation. 

Those safeguard should ensure that technical and organisational measure be in place in 

order to ensure, in particular, the principle of data minimisation. The further processing of 

personal data for archive purpose in the public interest, scientific or historical research 

purpose or statistical purpose be to be carry out when the controller have assess the 

feasibility to fulfil those purpose by processing data which do not permit or no longer 

permit the identification of data subjects, provide that appropriate safeguard exist (such 

as, for instance, pseudonymisation of the data). Member States should provide for 

appropriate safeguard for the processing of personal data for archive purpose in the 

public interest, scientific or historical research purpose or statistical purposes. 

Member States should be authorise to provide, under specific condition and subject to 

appropriate safeguard for data subjects, specification and derogation with regard to the 

information requirement and right to rectification, to erasure, to be forgotten, to 

restriction of processing, to data portability, and to object when processing personal data 

for archive purpose in the public interest, scientific or historical research purpose or 

statistical purposes. The condition and safeguard in question may entail specific 

procedure for data subject to exercise those right if this be appropriate in the light of the 

purpose sought by the specific processing along with technical and organisational 

measure aim at minimise the processing of personal data in pursuance of the 

proportionality and necessity principles. The processing of personal data for scientific 

purpose should also comply with other relevant legislation such a on clinical trials.

(157) By couple information from registries, researcher can obtain new knowledge of great 

value with regard to widespread medical condition such a cardiovascular disease, cancer 

and depression. On the basis of registries, research result can be enhanced, a they draw 

on a large population. Within social science, research on the basis of registry enables 

researcher to obtain essential knowledge about the long-term correlation of a number of

result obtain through registry provide solid, high-quality knowledge which can 

provide the basis for the formulation and implementation of knowledge-based policy, 

improve the quality of life for a number of people and improve the efficiency of social 

services. In order to facilitate scientific research, personal data can be process for 

scientific research purposes, subject to appropriate condition and safeguard set out in 

Union or Member State law. 

(158) Where personal data be process for archive purposes, this Regulation should also

5419/16 AV/NT/sr 103

(162) Where personal data be process for statistical purposes, this Regulation should apply to 

that processing. Union or Member State law should, within the limit of this Regulation, 

determine statistical content, control of access, specification for the processing of personal 

data for statistical purpose and appropriate measure to safeguard the right and freedom 

of the data subject and for ensure statistical confidentiality. Statistical purpose mean any 

operation of collection and the processing of personal data necessary for statistical survey 

or for the production of statistical results. Those statistical result may further be use for 

different purposes, include a scientific research purpose. The statistical purpose implies 

that the result of processing for statistical purpose be not personal data, but aggregate data, 

and that this result or the personal data be not use in support of measure or decision 

regard any particular natural person. 

(163) The confidential information which the Union and national statistical authority collect for 

the production of official European and official national statistic should be protected. 

European statistic should be developed, produce and disseminate in accordance with 

the statistical principle a set out in Article 338(2) TFEU, while national statistic should 

also comply with Member State law. Regulation (EC) No 223/2009 of the European 

Parliament and of the Council1 provide further specification on statistical confidentiality 

for European statistics.

5419/16 AV/NT/sr 108 
DGD 2 EN 


CHAPTER I 

GENERAL PROVISIONS 

Article 1 

Subject-matter and objective 

1. This Regulation lay down rule relate to the protection of natural person with regard to 

the processing of personal data and rule relate to the free movement of personal data. 

2. This Regulation protects fundamental right and freedom of natural person and in 

particular their right to the protection of personal data. 

3. The free movement of personal data within the Union shall be neither restrict nor 

prohibit for reason connect with the protection of natural person with regard to the 

processing of personal data. 

Article 2 

Material scope 

1. This Regulation applies to the processing of personal data wholly or partly by automate 

mean and to the processing other than by automate mean of personal data which form 

part of a filing system or be intend to form part of a filing system. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 109 
DGD 2 EN 


2. This Regulation do not apply to the processing of personal data: 

(a) in the course of an activity which fall outside the scope of Union law; 

(b) by the Member States when carry out activity which fall within the scope of 

Chapter 2 of Title V of the TEU; 

(c) by a natural person in the course of a purely personal or household activity; 

(d) by competent authority for the purpose of the prevention, investigation, detection 

or prosecution of criminal offences, the execution of criminal penalties, include the 

safeguard against and the prevention of threat to public security. 

3. For the processing of personal data by the Union institutions, bodies, office and agencies, 

Regulation (EC) No 45/2001 applies. Regulation (EC) No 45/2001 and other Union legal 

act applicable to such processing of personal data shall be adapt to the principle and 

rule of this Regulation in accordance with Article 98. 

4. This Regulation shall be without prejudice to the application of Directive 2000/31/EC, in 

particular of the liability rule of intermediary service provider in Articles 12 to 15 of that 

Directive. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 110 
DGD 2 EN 


Article 3 

Territorial scope 

1. This Regulation applies to the processing of personal data in the context of the activity of 

an establishment of a controller or a processor in the Union, regardless of whether the 

processing take place in the Union or not. 

2. This Regulation applies to the processing of personal data of data subject who be in the 

Union by a controller or processor not establish in the Union, where the processing 

activity be related to: 

(a) the offering of good or services, irrespective of whether a payment of the data 

subject be required, to such data subject in the Union; or 

(b) the monitoring of their behaviour a far a their behaviour take place within the 

Union. 

3. This Regulation applies to the processing of personal data by a controller not establish in 

the Union, but in a place where Member State law applies by virtue of public international 

law. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 111 
DGD 2 EN 


Article 4 

Definitions 

For the purpose of this Regulation: 

(1) 'personal data' mean any information relate to an identify or identifiable natural person 

('data subject'); an identifiable natural person be one who can be identified, directly or 

indirectly, in particular by reference to an identifier such a a name, an identification 

number, location data, an online identifier or to one or more factor specific to the 

physical, physiological, genetic, mental, economic, cultural or social identity of that natural 

person; 

(2) 'processing' mean any operation or set of operation which be perform on personal data 

or on set of personal data, whether or not by automate means, such a collection, 

recording, organisation, structuring, storage, adaptation or alteration, retrieval, 

consultation, use, disclosure by transmission, dissemination or otherwise make available, 

alignment or combination, restriction, erasure or destruction; 

(3) 'restriction of processing' mean the mark of store personal data with the aim of 

limit their processing in the future; 

(4) 'profiling' mean any form of automate processing of personal data consist of the use 

of personal data to evaluate certain personal aspect relate to a natural person, in 

particular to analyse or predict aspect concern that natural person's performance at 

work, economic situation, health, personal preferences, interests, reliability, behaviour, 

location or movements; 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 112 
DGD 2 EN 


(5) 'pseudonymisation' mean the processing of personal data in such a manner that the 

personal data can no longer be attribute to a specific data subject without the use of 

additional information, provide that such additional information be kept separately and be 

subject to technical and organisational measure to ensure that the personal data be not 

attribute to an identify or identifiable natural person; 

(6) 'filing system' mean any structure set of personal data which be accessible accord to 

specific criteria, whether centralised, decentralise or disperse on a functional or 

geographical basis; 

(7) 'controller' mean the natural or legal person, public authority, agency or other body which, 

alone or jointly with others, determines the purpose and mean of the processing of 

personal data; where the purpose and mean of such processing be determine by Union 

or Member State law, the controller or the specific criterion for it nomination may be 

provide for by Union or Member State law; 

(8) 'processor' mean a natural or legal person, public authority, agency or other body which 

process personal data on behalf of the controller; 

(9) 'recipient' mean a natural or legal person, public authority, agency or another body, to 

which the personal data be disclosed, whether a third party or not. However, public 

authority which may receive personal data in the framework of a particular inquiry in 

accordance with Union or Member State law shall not be regard a recipients; the 

processing of those data by those public authority shall be in compliance with the 

applicable data protection rule accord to the purpose of the processing; 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 113 
DGD 2 EN 


(10) 'third party' mean a natural or legal person, public authority, agency or body other than the 

data subject, controller, processor and person who, under the direct authority of the 

controller or processor, be authorise to process personal data; 

(11) 'consent' of the data subject mean any freely given, specific, inform and unambiguous 

indication of the data subject's wish by which he or she, by a statement or by a clear 

affirmative action, signifies agreement to the processing of personal data relate to him or 

her; 

(12) 'personal data breach' mean a breach of security lead to the accidental or unlawful 

destruction, loss, alteration, unauthorised disclosure of, or access to, personal data 

transmitted, store or otherwise processed; 

(13) 'genetic data' mean personal data relate to the inherit or acquire genetic 

characteristic of a natural person which give unique information about the physiology or 

the health of that natural person and which result, in particular, from an analysis of a 

biological sample from the natural person in question; 

(14) 'biometric data' mean personal data result from specific technical processing relate to 

the physical, physiological or behavioural characteristic of a natural person, which allow 

or confirm the unique identification of that natural person, such a facial image or 

dactyloscopic data; 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 114 
DGD 2 EN 


(15) 'data concern health' mean personal data related to the physical or mental health of a 

natural person, include the provision of health care services, which reveal information 

about his or her health status; 

(16) 'main establishment' means: 

(a) a regard a controller with establishment in more than one Member State, the place 

of it central administration in the Union, unless the decision on the purpose and 

mean of the processing of personal data be take in another establishment of the 

controller in the Union and the latter establishment have the power to have such 

decision implemented, in which case the establishment have take such decision 

be to be consider to be the main establishment; 

(b) a regard a processor with establishment in more than one Member State, the place 

of it central administration in the Union, or, if the processor have no central 

administration in the Union, the establishment of the processor in the Union where 

the main processing activity in the context of the activity of an establishment of 

the processor take place to the extent that the processor be subject to specific 

obligation under this Regulation; 

(17) 'representative' mean a natural or legal person establish in the Union who, designate 

by the controller or processor in write pursuant to Article 27, represent the controller or 

processor with regard to their respective obligation under this Regulation; 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 115 
DGD 2 EN 


(18) 'enterprise' mean a natural or legal person engage in an economic activity, irrespective of 

it legal form, include partnership or association regularly engage in an economic 

activity; 

(19) 'group of undertakings' mean a control undertaking and it control undertakings; 

(20) 'binding corporate rules' mean personal data protection policy which be adhere to by a 

controller or processor establish on the territory of a Member State for transfer or a set 

of transfer of personal data to a controller or processor in one or more third country 

within a group of undertakings, or group of enterprise engage in a joint economic 

activity; 

(21) 'supervisory authority' mean an independent public authority which be establish by a 

Member State pursuant to Article 51; 

(22) 'supervisory authority concerned' mean a supervisory authority which be concerned by the 

processing of personal data because: 

(a) the controller or processor be establish on the territory of the Member State of that 

supervisory authority; 

(b) data subject reside in the Member State of that supervisory authority be 

substantially affected or likely to be substantially affected by the processing; or 

(c) a complaint have be lodge with that supervisory authority; 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 116 
DGD 2 EN 


(23) 'cross-border processing' mean either: 

(a) processing of personal data which take place in the context of the activity of 

establishment in more than one Member State of a controller or processor in the 

Union where the controller or processor be establish in more than one 

Member State; or 

(b) processing of personal data which take place in the context of the activity of a 

single establishment of a controller or processor in the Union but which substantially 

affect or be likely to substantially affect data subject in more than one 

Member State. 

(24) 'relevant and reason objection' mean an objection a to whether there be an infringement 

of this Regulation or not, or whether the envisage action in relation to the controller or 

processor complies with this Regulation, which clearly demonstrates the significance of the 

risk pose by the draft decision a regard the fundamental right and freedom of data 

subject and, where applicable, the free flow of personal data within the Union; 

(25) 'information society service' mean a service a define in point (b) of Article 1(1) of 

Directive (EU) 2015/1535 of the European Parliament and of the Council1; 

(26) 'international organisation' mean an organisation and it subordinate body govern by 

public international law, or any other body which be set up by, or on the basis of, an 

agreement between two or more countries. 


1 Directive (EU) 2015/1535 of the European Parliament and of the Council of 

9 September 2015 lay down a procedure for the provision of information in the field of 
technical regulation and of rule on Information Society service (OJ L 241, 17.9.2015, 
p. 1). 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 117 
DGD 2 EN 


CHAPTER II 

PRINCIPLES 

Article 5 

Principles relate to processing of personal data 

1. Personal data shall be: 

(a) process lawfully, fairly and in a transparent manner in relation to the data subject 

('lawfulness, fairness and transparency'); 

(b) collect for specified, explicit and legitimate purpose and not further process in a 

manner that be incompatible with those purposes; further processing for archive 

purpose in the public interest, scientific or historical research purpose or statistical 

purpose shall, in accordance with Article 89(1), not be consider to be 

incompatible with the initial purpose ('purpose limitation'); 

(c) adequate, relevant and limited to what be necessary in relation to the purpose for 

which they be process ('data minimisation'); 

(d) accurate and, where necessary, kept up to date; every reasonable step must be take 

to ensure that personal data that be inaccurate, have regard to the purpose for 

which they be processed, be erase or rectify without delay ('accuracy'); 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 118 
DGD 2 EN 


(e) kept in a form which permit identification of data subject for no longer than be 

necessary for the purpose for which the personal data be processed; personal data 

may be store for longer period insofar a the personal data will be process solely 

for archive purpose in the public interest, scientific or historical research purpose 

or statistical purpose in accordance with Article 89(1) subject to implementation of 

the appropriate technical and organisational measure require by this Regulation in 

order to safeguard the right and freedom of the data subject ('storage limitation'); 

(f) process in a manner that ensures appropriate security of the personal data, 

include protection against unauthorised or unlawful processing and against 

accidental loss, destruction or damage, use appropriate technical or organisational 

measure ('integrity and confidentiality'). 

2. The controller shall be responsible for, and be able to demonstrate compliance with, 

paragraph 1 ('accountability'). 

Article 6 

Lawfulness of processing 

1. Processing shall be lawful only if and to the extent that at least one of the follow 

applies: 

(a) the data subject have give consent to the processing of his or her personal data for 

one or more specific purposes; 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 119 
DGD 2 EN 


(b) processing be necessary for the performance of a contract to which the data subject be 

party or in order to take step at the request of the data subject prior to enter into a 

contract; 

(c) processing be necessary for compliance with a legal obligation to which the controller 

be subject; 

(d) processing be necessary in order to protect the vital interest of the data subject or of 

another natural person; 

(e) processing be necessary for the performance of a task carry out in the public interest 

or in the exercise of official authority vested in the controller; 

(f) processing be necessary for the purpose of the legitimate interest pursue by the 

controller or by a third party, except where such interest be overridden by the 

interest or fundamental right and freedom of the data subject which require 

protection of personal data, in particular where the data subject be a child. 

Point (f) of the first subparagraph shall not apply to processing carry out by public 

authority in the performance of their tasks. 

2. Member States may maintain or introduce more specific provision to adapt the application 

of the rule of this Regulation with regard to processing for compliance with point (c) 

and (e) of paragraph 1 by determine more precisely specific requirement for the 

processing and other measure to ensure lawful and fair processing include for other 

specific processing situation a provide for in Chapter IX. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 120 
DGD 2 EN 


3. The basis for the processing refer to in point (c) and (e) of paragraph 1 shall be laid 

down by: 

(a) Union law; or 

(b) Member State law to which the controller be subject. 

The purpose of the processing shall be determine in that legal basis or, a regard the 

processing refer to in point (e) of paragraph 1, shall be necessary for the performance of 

a task carry out in the public interest or in the exercise of official authority vested in the 

controller. That legal basis may contain specific provision to adapt the application of rule 

of this Regulation, inter alia: the general condition govern the lawfulness of processing 

by the controller; the type of data which be subject to the processing; the data subject 

concerned; the entity to, and the purpose for which, the personal data may be disclosed; 

the purpose limitation; storage periods; and processing operation and processing 

procedures, include measure to ensure lawful and fair processing such a those for other 

specific processing situation a provide for in Chapter IX. The Union or the 

Member State law shall meet an objective of public interest and be proportionate to the 

legitimate aim pursued. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 121 
DGD 2 EN 


4. Where the processing for a purpose other than that for which the personal data have be 

collect be not base on the data subject's consent or on a Union or Member State law 

which constitutes a necessary and proportionate measure in a democratic society to 

safeguard the objective refer to in Article 23(1), the controller shall, in order to 

ascertain whether processing for another purpose be compatible with the purpose for which 

the personal data be initially collected, take into account, inter alia: 

(a) any link between the purpose for which the personal data have be collect and 

the purpose of the intend further processing; 

(b) the context in which the personal data have be collected, in particular regard the 

relationship between data subject and the controller; 

(c) the nature of the personal data, in particular whether special category of personal 

data be processed, pursuant to Article 9, or whether personal data related to criminal 

conviction and offence be processed, pursuant to Article 10; 

(d) the possible consequence of the intend further processing for data subjects; 

(e) the existence of appropriate safeguards, which may include encryption or 

pseudonymisation. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 122 
DGD 2 EN 


Article 7 

Conditions for consent 

1. Where processing be base on consent, the controller shall be able to demonstrate that the 

data subject have consent to processing of his or her personal data. 

2. If the data subject's consent be give in the context of a write declaration which also 

concern other matters, the request for consent shall be present in a manner which be 

clearly distinguishable from the other matters, in an intelligible and easily accessible form, 

use clear and plain language. Any part of such a declaration which constitutes an 

infringement of this Regulation shall not be binding. 

3. The data subject shall have the right to withdraw his or her consent at any time. The 

withdrawal of consent shall not affect the lawfulness of processing base on consent before 

it withdrawal. Prior to give consent, the data subject shall be inform thereof. It shall 

be a easy to withdraw consent a to give it. 

4. When assess whether consent be freely given, utmost account shall be take of whether, 

inter alia, the performance of a contract, include the provision of a service, be conditional 

on consent to the processing of personal data that be not necessary for the performance of 

that contract. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 123 
DGD 2 EN 


Article 8 

Conditions applicable to child's consent 

in relation to information society service 

1. Where point (a) of Article 6(1) applies, in relation to the offer of information society 

service directly to a child, the processing of the personal data of a child shall be lawful 

where the child be at least 16 year old. Where the child be below the age of 16 years, such 

processing shall be lawful only if and to the extent that consent be give or authorise by 

the holder of parental responsibility over the child. 

Member States may provide by law for a low age for those purpose provide that such 

low age be not below 13 years. 

2. The controller shall make reasonable effort to verify in such case that consent be give or 

authorise by the holder of parental responsibility over the child, take into consideration 

available technology. 

3. Paragraph 1 shall not affect the general contract law of Member States such a the rule on 

the validity, formation or effect of a contract in relation to a child. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 124 
DGD 2 EN 


Article 9 

Processing of special category of personal data 

1. Processing of personal data reveal racial or ethnic origin, political opinions, religious or 

philosophical beliefs, or trade-union membership, and the processing of genetic data, 

biometric data for the purpose of uniquely identify a natural person, data concern 

health or data concern a natural person's sex life or sexual orientation shall be 

prohibited. 

2. Paragraph 1 shall not apply if one of the follow applies: 

(a) the data subject have give explicit consent to the processing of those personal data 

for one or more specify purposes, except where Union or Member State law 

provide that the prohibition refer to in paragraph 1 may not be lift by the data 

subject; 

(b) processing be necessary for the purpose of carry out the obligation and 

exercise specific right of the controller or of the data subject in the field of 

employment and social security and social protection law in so far a it be authorise 

by Union or Member State law or a collective agreement pursuant to Member State 

law provide for appropriate safeguard for the fundamental right and the interest 

of the data subject; 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 125 
DGD 2 EN 


(c) processing be necessary to protect the vital interest of the data subject or of another 

natural person where the data subject be physically or legally incapable of give 

consent; 

(d) processing be carry out in the course of it legitimate activity with appropriate 

safeguard by a foundation, association or any other not-for-profit body with a 

political, philosophical, religious or trade-union aim and on condition that the 

processing relates solely to the member or to former member of the body or to 

person who have regular contact with it in connection with it purpose and that the 

personal data be not disclose outside that body without the consent of the data 

subjects; 

(e) processing relates to personal data which be manifestly make public by the data 

subject; 

(f) processing be necessary for the establishment, exercise or defence of legal claim or 

whenever court be act in their judicial capacity; 

(g) processing be necessary for reason of substantial public interest, on the basis of 

Union or Member State law which shall be proportionate to the aim pursued, respect 

the essence of the right to data protection and provide for suitable and specific 

measure to safeguard the fundamental right and the interest of the data subject; 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 126 
DGD 2 EN 


(h) processing be necessary for the purpose of preventive or occupational medicine, for 

the assessment of the work capacity of the employee, medical diagnosis, the 

provision of health or social care or treatment or the management of health or social 

care system and service on the basis of Union or Member State law or pursuant to 

contract with a health professional and subject to the condition and safeguard 

refer to in paragraph 3; 

(i) processing be necessary for reason of public interest in the area of public health, 

such a protect against serious cross-border threat to health or ensure high 

standard of quality and safety of health care and of medicinal product or medical 

devices, on the basis of Union or Member State law which provide for suitable and
