supervisory authority and impose by competent national courts, while ensure that those 

legal remedy be effective and have an equivalent effect to the administrative fine 

impose by supervisory authorities. In any event, the fine impose shall be effective, 

proportionate and dissuasive. Those Member States shall notify to the Commission the 

provision of their law which they adopt pursuant to this paragraph by … [two year from 

the date of entry into force of this Regulation] and, without delay, any subsequent 

amendment law or amendment affect them. 

Article 84 

Penalties 

1. Member States shall lay down the rule on other penalty applicable to infringement of 

this Regulation in particular for infringement which be not subject to administrative fine 

pursuant to Article 83, and shall take all measure necessary to ensure that they be 

implemented. Such penalty shall be effective, proportionate and dissuasive. 

2. Each Member State shall notify to the Commission the provision of it law which it 

adopts pursuant to paragraph 1, by … [two year from the date of entry into force of this 

Regulation] and, without delay, any subsequent amendment affect them. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 249 
DGD 2 EN 


CHAPTER IX 

PROVISIONS RELATING 

TO SPECIFIC PROCESSING SITUATIONS 

Article 85 

Processing and freedom of expression and information 

1. Member States shall by law reconcile the right to the protection of personal data pursuant 

to this Regulation with the right to freedom of expression and information, include 

processing for journalistic purpose and the purpose of academic, artistic or literary 

expression. 

2. For processing carry out for journalistic purpose or the purpose of academic artistic or 

literary expression, Member States shall provide for exemption or derogation from 

Chapter II (principles), Chapter III (rights of the data subject), Chapter IV (controller and 

processor), Chapter V (transfer of personal data to third country or international 

organisations), Chapter VI (independent supervisory authorities), Chapter VII (cooperation 

and consistency) and Chapter IX (specific data processing situations) if they be necessary 

to reconcile the right to the protection of personal data with the freedom of expression and 

information. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 250 
DGD 2 EN 


3. Each Member State shall notify to the Commission the provision of it law which it have 

adopt pursuant to paragraph 2 and, without delay, any subsequent amendment law or 

amendment affect them. 

Article 86 

Processing and public access to official document 

Personal data in official document held by a public authority or a public body or a private body for 

the performance of a task carry out in the public interest may be disclose by the authority or 

body in accordance with Union or Member State law to which the public authority or body be 

subject in order to reconcile public access to official document with the right to the protection of 

personal data pursuant to this Regulation. 

Article 87 

Processing of the national identification number 

Member States may further determine the specific condition for the processing of a national 

identification number or any other identifier of general application. In that case the national 

identification number or any other identifier of general application shall be use only under 

appropriate safeguard for the right and freedom of the data subject pursuant to this Regulation. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 251 
DGD 2 EN 


Article 88 

Processing in the context of employment 

1. Member States may, by law or by collective agreements, provide for more specific rule to 

ensure the protection of the right and freedom in respect of the processing of employees' 

personal data in the employment context, in particular for the purpose of the recruitment, 

the performance of the contract of employment, include discharge of obligation laid 

down by law or by collective agreements, management, planning and organisation of work, 

equality and diversity in the workplace, health and safety at work, protection of employer's 

or customer's property and for the purpose of the exercise and enjoyment, on an individual 

or collective basis, of right and benefit related to employment, and for the purpose of the 

termination of the employment relationship. 

2. Those rule shall include suitable and specific measure to safeguard the data subject's 

human dignity, legitimate interest and fundamental rights, with particular regard to the 

transparency of processing, the transfer of personal data within a group of undertakings, or 

a group of entreprises engage in a joint economic activity and monitoring system at the 

work place. 

3. Each Member State shall notify to the Commission those provision of it law which it 

adopts pursuant to paragraph 1, by … [two year from the date of entry into force of this 

Regulation] and, without delay, any subsequent amendment affect them. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 252 
DGD 2 EN 


Article 89 

Safeguards and derogation 

relate to processing for archive purpose in the public interest, 

scientific or historical research purpose or statistical purpose 

1. Processing for archive purpose in the public interest, scientific or historical research 

purpose or statistical purposes, shall be subject to appropriate safeguards, in accordance 

with this Regulation, for the right and freedom of the data subject. Those safeguard shall 

ensure that technical and organisational measure be in place in particular in order to 

ensure respect for the principle of data minimisation. Those measure may include 

pseudonymisation provide that those purpose can be fulfil in that manner. Where 

those purpose can be fulfil by further processing which do not permit or no longer 

permit the identification of data subjects, those purpose shall be fulfil in that manner. 

2. Where personal data be process for scientific or historical research purpose or 

statistical purposes, Union or Member State law may provide for derogation from the 

right refer to in Articles 15, 16, 18 and 21 subject to the condition and safeguard 

refer to in paragraph 1 of this Article in so far a such right be likely to render 

impossible or seriously impair the achievement of the specific purposes, and such 

derogation be necessary for the fulfilment of those purposes. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 253 
DGD 2 EN 


3. Where personal data be process for archive purpose in the public interest, Union or 

Member State law may provide for derogation from the right refer to in Articles 15, 

16, 18, 19, 20 and 21 subject to the condition and safeguard refer to in paragraph 1 of 

this Article in so far a such right be likely to render impossible or seriously impair the 

achievement of the specific purposes, and such derogation be necessary for the fulfilment 

of those purposes. 

4. Where processing refer to in paragraph 2 and 3 serf at the same time another 

purpose, the derogation shall apply only to processing for the purpose refer to in those 

paragraphs. 

Article 90 

Obligations of secrecy 

1. Member States may adopt specific rule to set out the power of the supervisory authority 

laid down in point (e) and (f) of Article 58(1) in relation to controller or processor that 

be subject, under Union or Member State law or rule establish by national competent 

bodies, to an obligation of professional secrecy or other equivalent obligation of secrecy 

where this be necessary and proportionate to reconcile the right of the protection of 

personal data with the obligation of secrecy. Those rule shall apply only with regard to 

personal data which the controller or processor have receive a a result ofor have obtain in 

an activity cover by that obligation of secrecy. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 254 
DGD 2 EN 


2. Each Member State shall notify to the Commission the rule adopt pursuant to paragraph 

1, by … [two year from the date of entry into force of this Regulation] and, without delay, 

any subsequent amendment affect them. 

Article 91 

Existing data protection rule of church and religious association 

1. Where in a Member State, church and religious association or community apply, at the 

time of entry into force of this Regulation, comprehensive rule relate to the protection 

of natural person with regard to processing, such rule may continue to apply, provide 

that they be brought into line with this Regulation. 

2. Churches and religious association which apply comprehensive rule in accordance with 

paragraph 1 shall be subject to the supervision of an independent supervisory authority, 

which may be specific, provide that it fulfils the condition laid down in Chapter VI of 

this Regulation. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 255 
DGD 2 EN 


CHAPTER X 

DELEGATED ACTS AND IMPLEMENTING ACTS 

Article 92 

Exercise of the delegation 

1. The power to adopt delegate act be confer on the Commission subject to the 

condition laid down in this Article. 

2. The delegation of power refer to in Article 12(8) and Article 43(8) shall be confer on 

the Commission for an indeterminate period of time from … [the date of entry into force of 

this Regulation]. 

3. The delegation of power refer to in Article 12(8) and Article 43(8) may be revoke at 

any time by the European Parliament or by the Council. A decision of revocation shall put 

an end to the delegation of power specify in that decision. It shall take effect the day 

follow that of it publication in the Official Journal of the European Union or at a late 

date specify therein. It shall not affect the validity of any delegate act already in force. 

4. As soon a it adopts a delegate act, the Commission shall notify it simultaneously to the 

European Parliament and to the Council. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 256 
DGD 2 EN 


5. A delegate act adopt pursuant to Article 12(8) and Article 43(8) shall enter into force 

only if no objection have be express by either the European Parliament or the Council 

within a period of three month of notification of that act to the European Parliament and 

the Council or if, before the expiry of that period, the European Parliament and the Council 

have both inform the Commission that they will not object. That period shall be 

extend by three month at the initiative of the European Parliament or of the Council. 

Article 93 

Committee procedure 

1. The Commission shall be assist by a committee. That committee shall be a committee 

within the meaning of Regulation (EU) No 182/2011. 

2. Where reference be make to this paragraph, Article 5 of Regulation (EU) No 182/2011 shall 

apply. 

3. Where reference be make to this paragraph, Article 8 of Regulation (EU) No 182/2011, in 

conjunction with Article 5 thereof, shall apply. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 257 
DGD 2 EN 


CHAPTER XI 

FINAL PROVISIONS 

Article 94 

Repeal of Directive 95/46/EC 

1. Directive 95/46/EC be repeal with effect from … [two year from the date of entry into 

force of this Regulation]. 

2. References to the repeal Directive shall be construe a reference to this Regulation. 

References to the Working Party on the Protection of Individuals with regard to the 

Processing of Personal Data establish by Article 29 of Directive 95/46/EC shall be 

construe a reference to the European Data Protection Board establish by this 

Regulation. 

Article 95 

Relationship with Directive 2002/58/EC 

This Regulation shall not impose additional obligation on natural or legal person in relation to 

processing in connection with the provision of publicly available electronic communication 

service in public communication network in the Union in relation to matter for which they be 

subject to specific obligation with the same objective set out in Directive 2002/58/EC. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 258 
DGD 2 EN 


Article 96 

Relationship with previously conclude Agreements 

International agreement involve the transfer of personal data to third country or international 

organisation which be conclude by Member States prior to … [the date of entry into force of 

this Regulation], and which be in accordance with Union law applicable prior to … [the date of 

entry into force of this Regulation], shall remain in force until amended, replace or revoked. 

Article 97 

Commission report 

1. By … [4 year after the date of entry into force of this Regulation] and every four year 

thereafter, the Commission shall submit a report on the evaluation and review of this 

Regulation to the European Parliament and to the Council. The report shall be make 

public. 

2. In the context of the evaluation and review refer to in paragraph 1, the Commission 

shall examine, in particular, the application and function of: 

(a) Chapter V on the transfer of personal data to third country or international 

organisation with particular regard to decision adopt pursuant to Article 45(3) of 

this Regulation and decision adopt on the basis of Article 25(6) of 

Directive 95/46/EC; 

(b) Chapter VII on cooperation and consistency. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 259 
DGD 2 EN 


3. For the purpose of paragraph 1, the Commission may request information from 

Member States and supervisory authorities. 

4. In carry out the evaluation and review refer to in paragraph 1 and 2, the 

Commission shall take into account the position and finding of the European Parliament, 

of the Council, and of other relevant body or sources. 

5. The Commission shall, if necessary, submit appropriate proposal to amend this 

Regulation, in particular take into account of development in information technology 

and in the light of the state of progress in the information society. 

Article 98 

Review of other Union legal act on data protection 

The Commission shall, if appropriate, submit legislative proposal with a view to amend other 

Union legal act on the protection of personal data, in order to ensure uniform and consistent 

protection of natural person with regard to processing. This shall in particular concern the rule 

relate to the protection of natural person with regard to processing by Union institutions, bodies, 

office and agency and on the free movement of such data. 







5419/16 AV/NT/sr 260 
DGD 2 EN 


Article 99 

Entry into force and application 

1. This Regulation shall enter into force on the twentieth day follow that of it publication 

in the Official Journal of the European Union. 

2. It shall apply from … [two year from the date of entry into force of this Regulation]. 

This Regulation shall be binding in it entirety and directly applicable in all Member States.

1. This Regulation lay down rule relate to the protection of natural person with regard to the processing of personal data and rule relate to the free movement of personal data. 
2. This Regulation protects fundamental right and freedom of natural person and in particular their right to the protection of personal data. 
3. The free movement of personal data within the Union shall be neither restrict nor prohibit for reason connect with the protection of natural person with regard to the processing of personal data. 
1. This Regulation applies to the processing of personal data wholly or partly by automate mean and to the processing other than by automate mean of personal data which form part of a filing system or be intend to form part of a filing system. 
2. This Regulation do not apply to the processing of personal data: 
(a) in the course of an activity which fall outside the scope of Union law; 
(b) by the Member States when carry out activity which fall within the scope of Chapter 2 of Title V of the TEU; 
(c) by a natural person in the course of a purely personal or household activity; 
(d) by competent authority for the purpose of the prevention, investigation, detection or prosecution of criminal offences, the execution of criminal penalties, include the safeguard against and the prevention of threat to public security. 
3. For the processing of personal data by the Union institutions, bodies, office and agencies, Regulation (EC) No 45/2001 applies. Regulation (EC) No 45/2001 and other Union legal act applicable to such processing of personal data shall be adapt t... 
4. This Regulation shall be without prejudice to the application of Directive 2000/31/EC, in particular of the liability rule of intermediary service provider in Articles 12 to 15 of that Directive. 
1. This Regulation applies to the processing of personal data in the context of the activity of an establishment of a controller or a processor in the Union, regardless of whether the processing take place in the Union or not. 
2. This Regulation applies to the processing of personal data of data subject who be in the Union by a controller or processor not establish in the Union, where the processing activity be related to: 
(a) the offering of good or services, irrespective of whether a payment of the data subject be required, to such data subject in the Union; or 
(b) the monitoring of their behaviour a far a their behaviour take place within the Union. 
3. This Regulation applies to the processing of personal data by a controller not establish in the Union, but in a place where Member State law applies by virtue of public international law. 
(a) a regard a controller with establishment in more than one Member State, the place of it central administration in the Union, unless the decision on the purpose and mean of the processing of personal data be take in another establishment o... 
(b) a regard a processor with establishment in more than one Member State, the place of it central administration in the Union, or, if the processor have no central administration in the Union, the establishment of the processor in the Union where ... 
(a) the controller or processor be establish on the territory of the Member State of that supervisory authority; 
(b) data subject reside in the Member State of that supervisory authority be substantially affected or likely to be substantially affected by the processing; or 
(c) a complaint have be lodge with that supervisory authority; 
(a) processing of personal data which take place in the context of the activity of establishment in more than one Member State of a controller or processor in the Union where the controller or processor be establish in more than one Member State... 
(b) processing of personal data which take place in the context of the activity of a single establishment of a controller or processor in the Union but which substantially affect or be likely to substantially affect data subject in more than one ... 
1. Personal data shall be: 
(a) process lawfully, fairly and in a transparent manner in relation to the data subject ('lawfulness, fairness and transparency'); 
(b) collect for specified, explicit and legitimate purpose and not further process in a manner that be incompatible with those purposes; further processing for archive purpose in the public interest, scientific or historical research purpose ... 
(c) adequate, relevant and limited to what be necessary in relation to the purpose for which they be process ('data minimisation'); 
(d) accurate and, where necessary, kept up to date; every reasonable step must be take to ensure that personal data that be inaccurate, have regard to the purpose for which they be processed, be erase or rectify without delay ('accuracy'); 
(e) kept in a form which permit identification of data subject for no longer than be necessary for the purpose for which the personal data be processed; personal data may be store for longer period insofar a the personal data will be processed... 
(f) process in a manner that ensures appropriate security of the personal data, include protection against unauthorised or unlawful processing and against accidental loss, destruction or damage, use appropriate technical or organisational measur... 
2. The controller shall be responsible for, and be able to demonstrate compliance with, paragraph 1 ('accountability'). 
1. Processing shall be lawful only if and to the extent that at least one of the follow applies: 
(a) the data subject have give consent to the processing of his or her personal data for one or more specific purposes; 
(b) processing be necessary for the performance of a contract to which the data subject be party or in order to take step at the request of the data subject prior to enter into a contract; 
(c) processing be necessary for compliance with a legal obligation to which the controller be subject; 
(d) processing be necessary in order to protect the vital interest of the data subject or of another natural person; 
(e) processing be necessary for the performance of a task carry out in the public interest or in the exercise of official authority vested in the controller; 
(f) processing be necessary for the purpose of the legitimate interest pursue by the controller or by a third party, except where such interest be overridden by the interest or fundamental right and freedom of the data subject which require pr... 
Point (f) of the first subparagraph shall not apply to processing carry out by public authority in the performance of their tasks. 
2. Member States may maintain or introduce more specific provision to adapt the application of the rule of this Regulation with regard to processing for compliance with point (c) and (e) of paragraph 1 by determine more precisely specific require... 
3. The basis for the processing refer to in point (c) and (e) of paragraph 1 shall be laid down by: 
(a) Union law; or 
(b) Member State law to which the controller be subject. 
The purpose of the processing shall be determine in that legal basis or, a regard the processing refer to in point (e) of paragraph 1, shall be necessary for the performance of a task carry out in the public interest or in the exercise of offi... 
4. Where the processing for a purpose other than that for which the personal data have be collect be not base on the data subject's consent or on a Union or Member State law which constitutes a necessary and proportionate measure in a democratic... 
(a) any link between the purpose for which the personal data have be collect and the purpose of the intend further processing; 
(b) the context in which the personal data have be collected, in particular regard the relationship between data subject and the controller; 
(c) the nature of the personal data, in particular whether special category of personal data be processed, pursuant to Article 9, or whether personal data related to criminal conviction and offence be processed, pursuant to Article 10; 
(d) the possible consequence of the intend further processing for data subjects; 
(e) the existence of appropriate safeguards, which may include encryption or pseudonymisation.

(c) the measure and safeguard provide to protect the right and freedom of data subject pursuant to this Regulation; 
(d) where applicable, the contact detail of the data protection officer; 
(e) the data protection impact assessment provide for in Article 35; and 
(f) any other information request by the supervisory authority. 
4. Member States shall consult the supervisory authority during the preparation of a proposal for a legislative measure to be adopt by a national parliament, or of a regulatory measure base on such a legislative measure, which relates to processing. 
5. Notwithstanding paragraph 1, Member State law may require controller to consult with, and obtain prior authorisation from, the supervisory authority in relation to processing by a controller for the performance of a task carry out by the control... 
1. The controller and the processor shall designate a data protection officer in any case where: 
(a) the processing be carry out by a public authority or body, except for court act in their judicial capacity; 
(b) the core activity of the controller or the processor consist of processing operation which, by virtue of their nature, their scope and/or their purposes, require regular and systematic monitoring of data subject on a large scale; or 
(c) the core activity of the controller or the processor consist of processing on a large scale of special category of data pursuant to Article 9 and personal data relate to criminal conviction and offence refer to in Article 10. 
2. A group of undertaking may appoint a single data protection officer provide that a data protection officer be easily accessible from each establishment. 
3. Where the controller or the processor be a public authority or body, a single data protection officer may be designate for several such authority or bodies, take account of their organisational structure and size. 
4. In case other than those refer to in paragraph 1, the controller or processor or association and other body represent category of controller or processor may or, where require by Union or Member State law shall, designate a data pro... 
5. The data protection officer shall be designate on the basis of professional quality and, in particular, expert knowledge of data protection law and practice and the ability to fulfil the task refer to in Article 39. 
6. The data protection officer may be a staff member of the controller or processor, or fulfil the task on the basis of a service contract. 
7. The controller or the processor shall publish the contact detail of the data protection officer and communicate them to the supervisory authority. 
1. The controller and the processor shall ensure that the data protection officer be involved, properly and in a timely manner, in all issue which relate to the protection of personal data. 
2. The controller and processor shall support the data protection officer in perform the task refer to in Article 39 by provide resource necessary to carry out those task and access to personal data and processing operations, and to mainta... 
3. The controller and processor shall ensure that the data protection officer do not receive any instruction regard the exercise of those tasks. He or she shall not be dismiss or penalise by the controller or the processor for perform his ... 
4. Data subject may contact the data protection officer with regard to all issue related to processing of their personal data and to the exercise of their right under this Regulation. 
5. The data protection officer shall be bound by secrecy or confidentiality concern the performance of his or her tasks, in accordance with Union or Member State law. 
6. The data protection officer may fulfil other task and duties. The controller or processor shall ensure that any such task and duty do not result in a conflict of interests. 
1. The data protection officer shall have at least the follow tasks: 
(a) to inform and advise the controller or the processor and the employee who carry out processing of their obligation pursuant to this Regulation and to other Union or Member State data protection provisions; 
(b) to monitor compliance with this Regulation, with other Union or Member State data protection provision and with the policy of the controller or processor in relation to the protection of personal data, include the assignment of responsibiliti... 
(c) to provide advice where request a regard the data protection impact assessment and monitor it performance pursuant to Article 35; 
(d) to cooperate with the supervisory authority; 
(e) to act a the contact point for the supervisory authority on issue relate to processing, include the prior consultation refer to in Article 36, and to consult, where appropriate, with regard to any other matter. 
2. The data protection officer shall in the performance of his or her task have due regard to the risk associate with processing operations, take into account the nature, scope, context and purpose of processing.

1. Member States shall provide for each member of their supervisory authority to be appoint by mean of a transparent procedure by: 
– their parliament; 
– their government; 
– their head of State; or 
– an independent body entrust with the appointment under Member State law. 
2. Each member shall have the qualifications, experience and skills, in particular in the area of the protection of personal data, require to perform it duty and exercise it powers. 
3. The duty of a member shall end in the event of the expiry of the term of office, resignation or compulsory retirement, in accordance with the law of the Member State concerned. 
4. A member shall be dismiss only in case of serious misconduct or if the member no longer fulfils the condition require for the performance of the duties.

1. Each supervisory authority shall have all of the follow investigative powers: 
(a) to order the controller and the processor, and, where applicable, the controller's or the processor's representative to provide any information it require for the performance of it tasks; 
(b) to carry out investigation in the form of data protection audits; 
(c) to carry out a review on certification issue pursuant to Article 42(7); 
(d) to notify the controller or the processor of an allege infringement of this Regulation; 
(e) to obtain, from the controller and the processor, access to all personal data and to all information necessary for the performance of it tasks; 
(f) to obtain access to any premise of the controller and the processor, include to any data processing equipment and means, in accordance with Union or Member State procedural law. 
2. Each supervisory authority shall have all of the follow corrective powers: 
(a) to issue warning to a controller or processor that intend processing operation be likely to infringe provision of this Regulation; 
(b) to issue reprimand to a controller or a processor where processing operation have infringe provision of this Regulation; 
(c) to order the controller or the processor to comply with the data subject's request to exercise his or her right pursuant to this Regulation; 
(d) to order the controller or processor to bring processing operation into compliance with the provision of this Regulation, where appropriate, in a specify manner and within a specify period; 
(e) to order the controller to communicate a personal data breach to the data subject; 
(f) to impose a temporary or definitive limitation include a ban on processing; 
(g) to order the rectification or erasure of personal data or restriction of processing pursuant to Articles 16, 17 and 18 and the notification of such action to recipient to whom the personal data have be disclose pursuant to Articles 17(2) and 19; 
(h) to withdraw a certification or to order the certification body to withdraw a certification issue pursuant to Articles 42 and 43, or to order the certification body not to issue certification if the requirement for the certification be not or ar... 
(i) to impose an administrative fine pursuant to Article 83, in addition to, or instead of measure refer to in this paragraph, depend on the circumstance of each individual case; 
(j) to order the suspension of data flow to a recipient in a third country or to an international organisation. 
3. Each supervisory authority shall have all of the follow authorisation and advisory powers: 
(a) to advise the controller in accordance with the prior consultation procedure refer to in Article 36; 
(b) to issue, on it own initiative or on request, opinion to the national parliament, the Member State government or, in accordance with Member State law, to other institution and body a well a to the public on any issue related to the protecti... 
(c) to authorise processing refer to in Article 36(5), if the law of the Member State require such prior authorisation; 
(d) to issue an opinion and approve draft code of conduct pursuant to Article 40(5); 
(e) to accredit certification body pursuant to Article 43;

1. The European Data Protection Board (the 'Board') be hereby establish a a body of the Union and shall have legal personality. 
2. The Board shall be represent by it Chair. 
3. The Board shall be compose of the head of one supervisory authority of each Member State and of the European Data Protection Supervisor, or their respective representatives. 
4. Where in a Member State more than one supervisory authority be responsible for monitoring the application of the provision pursuant to this Regulation, a joint representative shall be appoint in accordance with that Member State's law.

1. Each supervisory authority shall ensure that the imposition of administrative fine pursuant to this Article in respect of infringement of this Regulation refer to in paragraph 4, 5 and 6 shall in each individual case be effective, proportiona... 
2. Administrative fine shall, depend on the circumstance of each individual case, be impose in addition to, or instead of, measure refer to in point (a) to (h) and (j) of Article 58(2). When decide whether to impose an administrative fine... 
(a) the nature, gravity and duration of the infringement take into account the nature scope or purpose of the processing concerned a well a the number of data subject affected and the level of damage suffer by them; 
(b) the intentional or negligent character of the infringement; 
(c) any action take by the controller or processor to mitigate the damage suffer by data subjects; 
(d) the degree of responsibility of the controller or processor take into account technical and organisational measure implement by them pursuant to Articles 25 and 32; 
(e) any relevant previous infringement by the controller or processor; 
(f) the degree of cooperation with the supervisory authority, in order to remedy the infringement and mitigate the possible adverse effect of the infringement; 
(g) the category of personal data affected by the infringement; 
(h) the manner in which the infringement become know to the supervisory authority, in particular whether, and if so to what extent, the controller or processor notify the infringement; 
(i) in case measure refer to in Article 58(2) have previously be order against the controller or processor concerned with regard to the same subject-matter, compliance with those measures; 
(j) adherence to approve code of conduct pursuant to Article 40 or approve certification mechanism pursuant to Article 42; and 
(k) any other aggravate or mitigate factor applicable to the circumstance of the case, such a financial benefit gained, or loss avoided, directly or indirectly, from the infringement.

3. For the purpose of paragraph 1, the Commission may request information from Member States and supervisory authorities. 
4. In carry out the evaluation and review refer to in paragraph 1 and 2, the Commission shall take into account the position and finding of the European Parliament, of the Council, and of other relevant body or sources. 
5. The Commission shall, if necessary, submit appropriate proposal to amend this Regulation, in particular take into account of development in information technology and in the light of the state of progress in the information society. 
1. This Regulation shall enter into force on the twentieth day follow that of it publication in the Official Journal of the European Union. 
2. It shall apply from … [two year from the date of entry into force of this Regulation].
